# 06 - Decision Log

Append-only. One line per decision: date, decision, reason. Claude Code adds entries when a session makes a call; Matthew adds entries when product behavior is decided.

- 2026-07-06 | Deterministic rule-based scoring, AI narrative-only | Explainability and reproducibility are credibility requirements with advisors; avoids hallucination risk with financial clients.
- 2026-07-06 | Rubric stored as data with rubric_versions | Methodology will evolve; old assessments must stay comparable against their version.
- 2026-07-06 | Engagement (not deal) as core unit; immutable assessment snapshots | Clients are 12-36 months pre-deal; longitudinal score data is the compounding asset.
- 2026-07-06 | Multi-tenant RLS by firm from S2 | Advisor firms are the distribution channel; retrofitting tenancy is high-risk.
- 2026-07-06 | Advisor workspace before owner portal | Advisors drive adoption and revenue; owners can be served manually during pilot.
- 2026-07-06 | Sub-scores are a first-class table between questions and dimensions | DRS methodology scores derived metrics (HHI, CAGR, ratios), not raw answers; matches Blueprint II exactly.
- 2026-07-06 | DRS = six business dimensions only; owner-side questions form separate ORI | Per Blueprint II composite formula; owner/business divergence is itself a diagnostic output.
- 2026-07-06 | Discrete band scoring, no interpolation, in v1 | Hand-verifiability of fixtures; interpolation available later as rubric version bump.
- 2026-07-06 | HHI estimated from top-5 shares in v1 | Exact HHI requires Blueprint I data ingestion; proxy documented in seed README.
- 2026-07-06 | Unknown NRR scores 25 with a not-tracked flag | Not measuring is worse than measuring badly, but not zero; Matthew to ratify.
- 2026-07-06 | EBITDA recast, EV, value-gap dollars deferred to post-v1 | Methodology documented in docs/07; v1 ships scoring, gaps, roadmap, narrative.
- 2026-07-07 | Restricted dev/CI runs migrations on plain Postgres via db/supabase-shim.sql (auth schema, roles, auth.uid()) | Docker/supabase CLI unavailable in the build container; migrations stay Supabase-canonical, shim skipped on real Supabase.
- 2026-07-07 | Engine rounding replicates Python round-half-even on the exact binary double (pyRound) | Reference scorer used Python round; fixture 3 ORI (40.25 -> 40.2) is irreproducible with JS default rounding.
- 2026-07-07 | ORI sub-scores persist to sub_score_results like business sub-scores; fixture sub_scores maps cover business dims only | Explain trace and owner-readiness reporting need the stored parts; matches reference which tracks ORI separately.
- 2026-07-07 | Not-tracked flag text derived from sub-score code suffix (REV-NRR -> "NRR not tracked") | Matches reference fixture output; revisit if flags need per-sub-score copy.
- 2026-07-07 | Dev-only "Phase 1 verification" page runs the pure engine in-browser on bundled seed rubric + fixtures | Visual acceptance evidence for Phase 1; production scoring still reads rubric from db; page carries a DEV label.
- 2026-07-07 | Outcome capture schema (engagement_outcomes, append-only outcome_events) ships in v1 with no UI | The moat dataset cannot be built retroactively; recorded only from advisor-reported facts, never backfilled.
- 2026-07-07 | Assessment immutability preserved via supersede pattern (record_status + linkage, active_assessments read path); no in-place edits, ever | Corrections create a new scored assessment; column named record_status because status tracks the intake lifecycle.
- 2026-07-07 | Deltas are same-rubric-version only; cross-version comparison returns an explicit incomparable marker | Cross-version comparison deferred to a rescore-as-derived-data feature that never mutates the original snapshot.
- 2026-07-07 | Firm/advisor/owner provisioning is CLI-only (scripts/admin.ts) through MVP | Admin UI is out of scope until requested; S5 builds login + advisor shell only.
- 2026-07-07 | Demo tenant is seed data (seed/demo + scripts/seed-demo.ts), distinct from correctness fixtures | Demo tells the longitudinal story (59.9 Needs Work -> 72.3 Sale Ready, 6 gaps resolved); validated against the reference scorer inside the seed script, not the test suite.
- 2026-07-07 | Dev Supabase emulator (dev/supabase-dev-server.ts): Vite middleware implementing the auth/rest/functions surface the app uses, backed by local Postgres with real RLS per request | Same philosophy as db/supabase-shim.sql; app code is untouched supabase-js and runs against real Supabase in deploys; emulator is dev-only (fixed password), never bundled.
- 2026-07-07 | S7 "combined composite" rendered as a paired Business+Owner readout with divergence callout, not a blended number | CLAUDE.md rule 3a forbids mixing score groups; divergence is itself the diagnostic (2026-07-06 entry). A blended composite formula needs Matthew's ratification if ever wanted.
- 2026-07-07 | Narrative service uses claude-opus-4-8 with adaptive thinking; prompts forbid model arithmetic; ANTHROPIC_API_KEY server-side env only | Per docs/04 + S4.5 B2; injectable generator keeps tests key-free; strict numeral post-check regenerates once then fails loudly.
- 2026-07-07 | generated_documents.finalized_at added for edit-before-finalize | AI output stays a labeled draft until the advisor finalizes; print/PDF from the finalized view.
- 2026-07-07 | One-click demo: Codespaces badge on README + npm run dev:demo (scripts/dev-demo.sh boots db, migrations, seeds, demo advisor, Vite) | Instant way to open the local dev build; dev-only fixed password, real RLS via the dev emulator.
- 2026-07-09 | Owner report generates without a Claude API key via a deterministic composer (server/narrative.ts composeOwnerReport) | Rule-based narrative assembled from the same explain trace + gap set the scorer produced — no new numbers, nothing invented (CLAUDE.md rule 1/2 safe). Claude drafts when ANTHROPIC_API_KEY is set; otherwise the composer runs, labeled "Composed from your scores and flagged gaps". Report always generates.
- 2026-07-09 | Plain-language interpretation layer (shared/scoring/interpret.ts) is the single source of truth for turning scores/inputs/triggers into sentences | Used by both the results page and the report composer so they never drift. Adds no numbers and makes no scoring decisions — it phrases the deterministic output. Results page redesigned from a formula/matrix table to plain readings with quality bands, a "how scoring works" tier ladder, and plain gap reasons.
- 2026-07-09 | invokeFunction() unwraps the real edge-function error message instead of the generic "non-2xx status code" | Users (and advisors) see why generation/scoring failed rather than an opaque wrapper.
- 2026-07-09 | Full light + dark theme on a semantic design-token system (src/styles.css, src/lib/theme.tsx) | Every component reads from tokens so both themes stay in sync; deep-navy advisory identity. Theme defaults to system preference, is toggleable in the shell + login header, persists to localStorage, and is set pre-paint by an inline script in index.html to avoid flash. Could not reach exitblueprint.net from the build environment (agent proxy 403) to match the marketing site exactly.
- 2026-07-10 | Intake redesigned for zero-friction data entry (src/pages/IntakePage.tsx + src/lib/intakeFields.ts) while the stored answer format is unchanged | Presentation-only metadata layer (intakeFields.ts) maps question codes to unit adornments ($/%/months/hrs), labeled per-item list rows (top-5 customer shares, four-year revenue), humanized option labels, and 1-5 scale anchors parsed from the prompt. Lists render as labeled rows instead of a comma box; numbers show inline unit affixes and a live "$1,234,000" hint; short option sets render as cards, longer ones as a styled dropdown; numeric-or-unknown gets a "Not tracked" toggle. A progress bar counts answered scored questions and step chips are clickable. Answer values persisted to the DB are still numbers/number arrays/option strings/1-5/"unknown", so scoring is untouched — the e2e walkthrough reproduces company-1 exactly (DRS 82.6, Sale Ready, ORI 79.2).
- 2026-07-10 | Scenario Workbench (src/pages/WorkbenchPage.tsx): advisors edit any answer and every score updates in real time, computed in the browser by the shared engine (explainFromAnswers) — zero server round-trip, byte-for-byte identical to server scoring | Answers are held in browser state as a what-if; the source assessment is never mutated (CLAUDE.md rule 4). "Save as new assessment" persists a scenario as a new immutable assessment (next sequence, same rubric version) and scores it via the existing score-assessment path. The board shows DRS/ORI/dimension/gap deltas vs. the saved baseline. Rubric read client-side via loadEngineRubric (RLS methodology_read makes rubric tables world-readable to authenticated users).
- 2026-07-10 | Intake answer controls extracted to src/lib/answerFields.tsx and shared by intake + workbench | One editor, one Draft/toAnswerValue contract so the two surfaces cannot drift; stored answer format unchanged. Engagement page gains a DRS trajectory across assessments so the longitudinal story is visible in one place.
- 2026-07-11 | F0 design system: forest/green institutional palette on the existing token layer | Retheme of src/styles.css from navy to deep forest (brand #16352a, accent #1f7a52, buttons #1b4a38) plus a typed token module (src/lib/tokens.ts) and one shared formatter (src/lib/format.ts) for scores/deltas/currency/dates. Per-firm branding overrides --accent on client-facing views (one variable swap). Fonts are system stacks (Inter/Inter Tight → system-ui) with tabular numerals — no web-font network dependency, keeping the app offline/CI-safe.
- 2026-07-11 | Five DRS tiers get one fixed color each, validated with the dataviz palette validator, used everywhere (chips, dials, charts, PDFs) | Light: Not Saleable #c0362c, High Risk #e0670f, Needs Work #9a7d0a, Sale Ready #2f9e44, Institutional Grade #0e8f9e (teal, deliberately distinct from brand green). Dark variants brighter for the dark surface. Tiers are an ordinal, always-labeled scale — color is never the sole cue (TierBadge always prints the name), so the warm red/orange/amber CVD adjacency is acceptable; all five pass contrast ≥3:1 with monotonic lightness.
- 2026-07-11 | F0 component library (src/components/ui) + dev gallery at /dev/components | ScoreDial, TierBadge, DeltaChip, TrajectoryChart (signature SVG line+area with tier-colored points, supersede markers, dashed target line), DimensionBars, DataTable (sortable/sticky/loading/empty/error), PageHeader, Card, StatBlock, EmptyState, Timeline, FirmMark, Skeleton, ConfirmDialog, Toast. All token-driven; light+dark verified by screenshot.
- 2026-07-11 | F0 data layer: TanStack Query v5 with a central key registry (src/lib/queries.ts) | Clients, Engagement, Results, Report, and Intake pages migrated off ad-hoc supabase-js reads to typed query hooks; mutations invalidate precise keys. WorkbenchPage retains its bespoke Promise.all bootstrap for now (it drives byte-identical client-side scoring; migrating it was deferred to avoid destabilizing that path). Health/Verify are dev/internal surfaces.
- 2026-07-11 | F1 firm branding: firm_branding table (one row/firm), advisor-writable, firm-member-readable | Migration 20260711000100 (additive). accent_color has a hex CHECK; RLS: firm_member_read (advisors + owners) and advisor_firm_write. rls-test extended (+5 assertions → 21/21): advisor creates/reads own, cannot modify firm B; owner reads own firm branding, cannot write. BrandingProvider overrides --accent for the subtree; FirmMark renders logo-or-initial + name; the advisor's firm is the face, "Powered by Exit Blueprint" is discreet. Applied to the shell header and the owner-report header/footer. Logo stored as URL or data URI (dev has no storage bucket; production can swap to Supabase Storage). Demo seed brands the demo firm as "Cascade Wealth Partners".
- 2026-07-12 | F2 advisor portfolio dashboard is the new home (/); Clients moved to /clients | usePortfolio() assembles one cached view of the firm's book (latest active-completed assessment per engagement, prior-vs-latest delta, sparkline points, open-gap counts, days-since-last staleness) client-side from four RLS-scoped reads — no new view/migration. Stale (≥90d) and negative-delta rows are visually prominent; sort/filter by tier, movement, staleness. scripts/seed-portfolio.ts populates the demo firm with N engagements built from the real fixtures and scored by the engine, so dashboard rows and click-through are genuine (not synthetic score rows). Page container widened to 1140px for table density.
- 2026-07-12 | F3 engagement command view redesign | One page: branded header + outcome status, signature TrajectoryChart with a Competitive-Process-Ready target line (DRS 85, docs/07), current-assessment ScoreDial + DimensionBars, open gaps joined to their mapped playbooks, a compare-any-two panel, an assessments list, and documents/tasks sections (tasks empty until F5). Compare is exposed as a real function: compareAssessments wired into the dev emulator as 'compare-assessments' (authorizes both assessment ids through RLS, then runs on a service connection); the panel renders same-version deltas and the explicit incomparable marker, never a fabricated cross-version number. No mutation of completed assessments from this page.
- 2026-07-12 | F4 branded delta report end-to-end (new doc_type delta_report) | Additive enum migration (ALTER TYPE ADD VALUE, transactional on PG16). Server buildDeltaReportPayload runs compareAssessments(prior, current) where prior is the preceding active-completed assessment; no prior or a different rubric version → Baseline mode (levels, never a fabricated change). Narrative via Claude (prompts/delta_report.v1.md) with the same numeral firewall, or a deterministic composeDeltaReport fallback; counts live in the payload so neither path self-computes a number. Server-side HTML→PDF via Playwright (server/pdf.ts renderDeltaReportHtml + renderReportPdf, chromium resolved from EB_CHROMIUM_PATH) — a 3-section print-first branded layout (firm logo/from-line, DRS movement, dimension delta table, gaps resolved/opened, disclosure + Powered-by footer), exposed as the 'render-delta-pdf' binary function; the frontend downloads the Blob. NOT window.print(). DeltaReportPage: pick the as-of assessment → generate → WYSIWYG branded preview → edit narrative → finalize → download PDF. Verified live: a valid 2-page branded PDF rendered from the demo engagement.
- 2026-07-12 | Advisory Library: one catalog (advisory_library_items) unifying buyer_question / initiative / risk_flag, firing off live persisted scores | Migration 20260712000200 (additive; enums advisory_item_type, advisory_source). Global-vs-tenant decided explicitly (audit debt #8): system-curated rows are GLOBAL (firm_id null, readable by everyone like methodology, service_role-write only); advisor-authored rows are TENANT-scoped (firm_id set, firm-isolated RLS). Partial unique index on code where firm_id is null keeps system seeding idempotent. server/advisory.ts fireAdvisoryItems(db, engagementId) reads the latest completed assessment's dimension_scores + sub_score_results verbatim and surfaces catalog items whose governing score (sub_score_code if set, else dimension_code) is ≤ score_trigger, sorted critical-first then lowest-score-first — descriptive only, never computes or adjusts a score, DRS engine stays byte-identical. Exposed as the 'advisory-items' dev function. Seed: seed/advisory-library.csv, 28 curated system items (10 buyer questions, 10 initiatives, 8 risk flags) wired to the same sub-score triggers as the gap rubric. UI: /library catalog (filter by type/dimension/text, source badges, advisor CRUD for firm items) and /engagement/:id/buyer-lens (three lenses grouped, critical-first, live score vs trigger, expandable preparation/documentation). rls-test extended (+7 → 32/32); tests/advisory.test.ts (+5) locks firing order and firm/global visibility.
- 2026-07-13 | Phase 1 (foundation): financial provenance & verification (answer_provenance) | Migration 20260713000100 (additive; enum provenance_source self_reported|document|connected_ledger). Records where each financial answer came from; server/verification.ts verificationSummary derives the document-verified % over the scored FIN+REV questions (document/ledger = verified, self_reported = not), with default tier thresholds (≥67 document_verified, ≥34 partly_verified) that are a product decision to finalize. Purely descriptive — never reads or writes a score; the DRS stays byte-identical. Exposed as the 'verification-summary' dev function. UI: a VerificationCard on the engagement view (per-input source selector + tier badge + bar) and a "% verified" chip by the DRS dial. The connected_ledger source is a manual stand-in until the QuickBooks/Xero OAuth connect + auto-ingestion land (next Phase 1 slice; needs external OAuth infra). RLS: advisor firm-scoped CRUD, owner reads own company's rows; rls-test +3 (35/35). tests/verification.test.ts (+3) locks the tier thresholds and the verified-count logic.
- 2026-07-13 | Phase 3 (start): owner portal — login infrastructure, QB/Xero connection, education, and read access to the advisor's work | Owners already had RLS read access to their company's completed assessments, results, gaps, tasks, milestones, owner reports, branding, provenance, and world-readable content_modules; this adds the owner-facing surface. Role-aware routing: RequireOwner guard + a branded OwnerShell; RequireAdvisor now redirects owners to /portal. Pages: /portal (readiness home — DRS/ORI/verified%, plain-language tier, top gaps, workspace links), /portal/plan (read-only roadmap tasks + milestones), /portal/learn (content_modules, ones tied to open gaps via gap_content_map flagged "recommended"), /portal/documents (owner_report reports: read inline + download via render-owner-pdf), /portal/connect (QuickBooks/Xero). New migration ledger_connections (provider/status + org name), the connection-state model the real OAuth handshake would write and the verification layer reads; unusually, owners get write access scoped to their own company (they control their books connection). The OAuth handshake itself is external — the connect flow records the connection it would create (manual stand-in), same posture as Phase 1's connected_ledger provenance. RLS: advisor firm CRUD + owner own-company CRUD; rls-test +3 (38/38: advisor/owner ledger isolation, owner can connect own). The portal is branded as the advisor's firm (BrandingProvider), consistent with the reports.
- 2026-07-13 | Learn content unified into the Advisory Library (new item_type 'education') | Migration 20260713000300 (ALTER TYPE advisory_item_type ADD VALUE 'education'). Education pieces now live in advisory_library_items and fire off the same score triggers as buyer questions / initiatives / risk flags — an education guide is "recommended for you" when its governing sub-score/dimension is at or below its score_trigger. Advisors author and filter them in /library (Education added to the type dropdown + filter); owners read them in /portal/learn. server/advisory.ts educationModules(engagementId) returns all education items visible to the firm (system + firm) with a recommended flag computed from the live scores; fireAdvisoryItems now excludes item_type='education' so the advisor buyer-lens is unaffected. Exposed as the 'education-modules' dev function; the owner Learn page moved off content_modules/gap_content_map onto it (useEducation removed). Seed: 7 curated system education pieces in advisory-library.csv (untriggered general guides + ones tied to OPS-HOURS/CUS-TOP1/FIN-ADDBACK/OPS-SOP/REV-RECUR). tests/advisory.test.ts +2 (education firing + advisor-firing exclusion); 64 tests green.
- 2026-07-13 | QuickBooks/Xero ledger sync fills financial assessment answers | server/ledger.ts isolates the (external) accounting API behind pullLedgerFinancials; syncLedgerToAssessment fills the ledger-derivable questions (REV-ANNUAL, REV-TOP5-SHARES, REV-RECUR-PCT, FIN-RECON, FIN-BASIS, FIN-STATEMENTS — 6 of the 10 financial inputs; contract terms, NRR, and add-back judgment stay manual) into an in-progress assessment's answers and marks each connected_ledger provenance, lifting the verification %. The dev adapter derives deterministic, internally consistent figures from the company's books (most-recent answered figures where present, else stable defaults) so the flow works without live OAuth; swapping in the real Intuit/Xero API is confined to pullLedgerFinancials. Exposed as the 'sync-ledger' dev function (advisor-triggered — owner RLS can't see the in-progress assessment). Intake: an "Import from QuickBooks" banner (shown when the company has a connected ledger), a "✓ from QuickBooks" badge on filled questions (via useAnswerProvenance), and provenance auto-downgrades to self_reported when a synced figure is hand-edited (saveStep deletes the provenance row for any changed ledger/document answer) so the verified % stays honest. Nothing is forced — non-derivable questions and manual override remain fully available. tests/ledger.test.ts (+4): fills+provenance+verification, idempotent, refuses without a connection or on a completed assessment. 68 tests green.
- 2026-07-13 | Phase 2 valuation methodology (Matthew's decisions) | (1) Method: market multiple of adjusted (recast) EBITDA. (2) Multiple: industry×size base, scaled by DRS readiness and range-width by verification tier. (3) Net-to-owner: simple configurable model EV − debt − transaction costs − taxes. (4) Seed proposed starter numbers, versioned for later refinement. Starters (illustrative, editable via valuation_rules_version): multiple table field_services 3.5/4.5/5.0, manufacturing 4.0/5.0/5.5, distribution 3.5/4.5/5.0, healthcare 4.5/5.5/6.5, software 5.0/7.0/9.0, default 3.5/4.5/5.0 (size bands <1M / 1-3M / 3-5M adj EBITDA; >5M = 3-5M); readiness adj by DRS tier 1.15/1.0/0.85/0.70/0.55; verification range width ±10/20/30%; transaction cost 8% of EV; blended tax 28% of gain; target DRS 85 for the value-creation gap. Deterministic: valuation_rules compute the number, AI only narrates. Value gaps: value-creation (potential EV at DRS 85 − current) and wealth (owner target − net proceeds).
- 2026-07-13 | Ledger connections over real OAuth (QuickBooks/Xero) + the outcome-calibration moat | Two threads. (A) Connection workflow fixed to a real OAuth 2.0 shape with a dev fallback: migration 20260713000600 adds a service-only ledger_credentials table (tokens, NO grant to authenticated — a client JWT can never read a token, RLS or not), a ledger_oauth_states pending table (CSRF + return path), and realm_id/disconnected_at on ledger_connections. server/ledger-oauth.ts exposes begin → complete → disconnect: begin persists a state and returns the provider authorize URL (env-driven; providerConfig reads QUICKBOOKS_*/XERO_*/LEDGER_OAUTH_REDIRECT_URI), complete exchanges the code for tokens (or synthesizes them in dev when no app is configured) and upserts the connection, disconnect revokes best-effort and flips status to 'disconnected' (row kept for history, tokens wiped). Both surfaces now drive the same three functions via a shared useLedgerActions hook, so owner (OwnerConnectPage) and advisor (AccountingCard) never diverge; disconnect flips status instead of deleting, and the UI gates on status==='connected'. New /ledger/callback route (RequireAuth) completes the real handshake. Dev functions ledger-connect-begin/complete/disconnect are company-scoped (authorized via companies RLS; complete resolves the company from the opaque state). rls-test +3 (44/44: tokens quarantined from both roles). tests/ledger-oauth.test.ts (+6) locks the dev lifecycle. (B) Moat infrastructure (docs/09-moats.md): migration 20260713000700 adds deal_outcomes — one advisor-reported record per closed/broken engagement tying the PREDICTION (DRS/ORI/verified%/predicted EV range, snapshotted at record time from the latest completed assessment + valuation engine) to REALITY (final EV, multiple, EBITDA, buyer type, structure, retrade, days on market, buyer-flagged risks). Reality is fact never inferred; the snapshot freezes what we predicted; calibration reads these rows and never writes a score (a recalibration ships as a new rubric/valuation version). server/outcomes.ts: recordDealOutcome (idempotent per engagement) + firmCalibration (predicted-vs-actual: within-range hit rate, EV variance, avg multiple, retrade rate). DealOutcomeCard on the engagement view captures it; CalibrationPanel on the portfolio dashboard reports it. RLS advisor-firm-only (the firm's internal asset, not owner-portal content). tests/outcomes.test.ts (+3) locks the snapshot + calibration math against the valuation engine. 83 tests green.
- 2026-07-13 | Going-live topology: Vercel (frontend) + Supabase (data/auth) + Render (compute) | Added vercel.json (framework vite, build `npm run build`, output dist, SPA rewrite → index.html so client-router deep links don't 404) and docs/12-vercel-supabase-setup.md, a click-by-click companion to the docs/11 runbook for the specific Vercel+Supabase+GitHub case. Key point made explicit: the app is three runtime pieces, not two — the compute service (server/http.ts, /functions/v1/*, PDF via Chromium in server/Dockerfile) is a long-lived container and belongs on Render/Railway/Fly, NOT Vercel serverless; deploy order Supabase→Render→Vercel then a CORS/redeploy pass. Env split documented (VITE_* on Vercel baked at build time; DATABASE_URL/FUNCTIONS_JWT_SECRET/FUNCTIONS_ALLOWED_ORIGIN/ANTHROPIC_API_KEY on Render). Flagged the JWT signing-key caveat (HS256 path won't validate asymmetric-signed tokens) as a pre-launch follow-up. No code/schema/scoring change — config + docs only.
- 2026-07-14 | Compute service verifies both HS256 and asymmetric (JWKS) Supabase tokens | server/auth-jwt.ts (new, using jose) replaces the hand-rolled HS256 check in server/http.ts. makeVerifyToken inspects each token's `alg` header and routes it: HS256 → the legacy shared secret (FUNCTIONS_JWT_SECRET), ES256/RS256/EdDSA → the project JWKS at <SUPABASE_URL>/auth/v1/.well-known/jwks.json (createRemoteJWKSet, fetched+cached). Supporting both — not swapping — keeps a project working mid rotation; the token's alg picks the path. Startup now requires at least one of FUNCTIONS_JWT_SECRET / SUPABASE_URL (refuses to boot otherwise). jwtVerify enforces signature+exp; we additionally require a string `sub`. Verification is isolated behind a test seam (config.jwks) so tests/auth-jwt.test.ts (+8, pure crypto, no DB) exercises the asymmetric path with a local JWKS and covers wrong-key/expired/no-sub/malformed/mixed-mode rejection. Docs updated: docs/11 §2a, docs/12 env tables, server/Dockerfile env comment. No scoring/schema change; the DRS is untouched. NOTE: the reported client login error "The string did not match the expected pattern" is a browser-side DOMException in supabase-js's fetch/WebCrypto path (not this service and not our code) — almost certainly a Vercel env-var misconfig (unset/whitespace VITE_SUPABASE_URL/KEY, needs redeploy) or a stale localStorage session; diagnosis pending the browser stack trace.
- 2026-07-14 | Trim VITE_SUPABASE_* / VITE_FUNCTIONS_URL env values in src/lib/supabase.ts | Mitigates the reported Safari/iOS login failure "The string did not match the expected pattern": a trailing newline/space pasted into Vercel's env-var UI rides into the request URL and apikey header, and WebKit rejects it when building the request (Chromium is more lenient, so it only showed on iOS). A URL/Supabase key never has meaningful surrounding whitespace, so trimming is safe. isDevStack now keys off the trimmed URL too, so a whitespace-only value doesn't read as "configured". Config-hygiene only; no behavior change for correct values.
- 2026-07-14 | Bridge the Supabase↔Vercel integration's public vars into VITE_ names + render.yaml blueprint | (A) vite.config.ts bridges NEXT_PUBLIC_SUPABASE_URL/SUPABASE_URL → VITE_SUPABASE_URL and NEXT_PUBLIC_SUPABASE_ANON_KEY/SUPABASE_ANON_KEY/PUBLISHABLE variants → VITE_SUPABASE_ANON_KEY at build time (only if the VITE_ name isn't already set). The native integration injects credentials under Next.js/generic names, but Vite only exposes VITE_-prefixed vars to the client, so the integration "connected" yet the frontend saw nothing and login broke; the bridge makes it work with zero hand-added frontend env vars. Strictly the two PUBLIC values — the service-role key and JWT secret are never bridged into the browser bundle. Verified: a build with only NEXT_PUBLIC_SUPABASE_URL set bakes that URL into dist. VITE_FUNCTIONS_URL still must be set by hand (no integration can know the Render URL). (B) render.yaml (Render Blueprint) makes the compute service one-click deployable from the repo: docker runtime, server/Dockerfile, /health check, plan standard (2GB — headless Chromium PDF wants the memory; starter can OOM), and the env vars as sync:false prompts (DATABASE_URL, SUPABASE_URL/FUNCTIONS_JWT_SECRET, FUNCTIONS_ALLOWED_ORIGIN, ANTHROPIC_API_KEY). Docs/12 updated with both. Config/docs only; no scoring/schema change.
- 2026-07-15 | Advisor UX cleanup: engagement command view reorganized for hierarchy + a shared Collapsible primitive | The engagement page was a flat wall of ~12 cards with administrative plumbing (owner access, accounting connect, financial verification, deal outcome) rendered *before* the actual readiness picture, and four sub-tool links crowding the header. Reordered so the advisor sees the decision-making story first — current-readiness snapshot + open gaps, then the exit-pace trajectory, score drivers, and compare — moved the four sub-tool links into a single labeled "Workspace" toolbar row, and folded the setup/admin cards into a new default-collapsed `Collapsible` (native `<details>`, keyboard-accessible, token-styled; src/components/ui/Collapsible.tsx). - 2026-07-15 | Fix PDF export in local dev + cross-platform Chromium resolution; cap the scenario-workbench board to the viewport | (1) PDF: resolveChromium (server/pdf.ts) only searched Linux cache/system paths (/opt/pw-browsers, /usr/bin/chromium…), so `npm run dev` on a Mac/Windows workstation — where playwright-core ships no browser and a local `npx playwright install` caches under ~/Library/Caches/ms-playwright (macOS), ~/.cache/ms-playwright (Linux), or %USERPROFILE%\AppData\Local\ms-playwright (Windows) — found nothing and the download surfaced "could not launch Chromium". Now scans all per-OS Playwright caches (via findChromiumInCache, which understands chrome-linux/chrome-mac/chrome-win layouts) and common Google Chrome / Chromium / Edge install paths on macOS + Windows; launch error now points devs at `npx playwright install chromium`. tests/pdf.test.ts +3 (synthesized cache layouts). (2) invokeFunctionBlob (src/lib/supabase.ts) now rejects a 200 that isn't a PDF/octet-stream — a misconfigured VITE_FUNCTIONS_URL pointing at the SPA host returned index.html with 200 and it downloaded as a broken .pdf silently; now a clear error. (3) Workbench: .wb-board was position:sticky with no height cap, so a board taller than the viewport had its lower half clipped off-screen on scroll; capped to max-height:calc(100vh-2rem) with internal overflow-y (reverting to static/no-cap under the 900px single-column breakpoint), and tightened the hero number/padding so it fits without scrolling in the common case. Presentation + dev-tooling only; no scoring/schema/product-behavior change.

- 2026-07-16 | Beta Requirement 5 (security baseline): encryption at rest, signed document URLs, access audit log, MFA, security one-pager | (1) Encryption at rest: document bytes are AES-256-GCM encrypted before storage (server/documents/crypto.ts, key from EB_DOCUMENT_KEY with a documented weak dev default); document_blobs.enc_algo tags the envelope so legacy plaintext rows still read. - 2026-07-16 | Sell-side intelligence substrate (foundation slice): document-verified knowledge graph, reconciliation, resumable pipeline, findings container, LLM cost ledger | Scaffolds the service layer that turns scored self-assessment into document-verified sell-side intelligence. Deliberately built INSIDE existing conventions (npm single-package, server/ + shared/ + supabase/migrations, the existing ParserAdapter seam) rather than the prompt's literal pnpm /packages monorepo — the repo already implements much of the prompt's surface (ParserAdapter, a document intake+review pipeline, engagements/documents/document_fields/field_corrections, a deterministic scorer), so a restructure would duplicate working seams and break CI/deploy. Confirmed this fork with Matthew before building. Scope this pass is the FOUNDATION only (migrations + schemas + job runner + ontology container + one pipeline vertical through reconcile, all green on fixtures); later steps are declared but stubbed. (1) Migration 20260716000500 adds net-new tables only — graph_nodes/graph_edges (relational graph, JSONB attributes, temporal valid_from/valid_to), assessment_values (self-reported vs document-verified reconciliation with evidence_fact_id provenance), findings (buy-side patterns in reverse, graph_evidence + AI-draft-then-approve), scores (raw|verified, deterministic engine only), jobs (resumable pipeline state, no Temporal), review_items (generalized queue distinct from the per-field field_corrections log), llm_calls (per-call cost ledger) — every table firm_id + staff_firm_all RLS matching the documents layer; rls-test +7 (61 total). document_fields is REUSED as the extracted-facts substrate, extended additively with node_id/source_page/source_span/extraction_run_id (node_id + evidence_fact_id are ON DELETE SET NULL so idempotent rebuilds don't trip FKs). (2) Ontology lives in DATA (seed/ontology/business-ontology.json) behind a registry/loader (server/ontology/registry.ts) that validates node/edge types + attributes — the container the prior repo's ontology ports into, no ontology logic in code. (3) Job runner (server/pipeline/) drives a job through intake→parse→extract→populate_graph→reconcile (implemented, idempotent, checkpointed) and parks at score→match_findings→assemble→deliver (declared, throw NotImplementedError) for later slices; parse reuses resolveParser with a new FixtureParserAdapter (EB_PARSER=fixture) that returns fixture JSON — the prompt's "stub adapter that returns fixtures". reconcile auto-resolves confident agreements and queues conflicts/low-confidence to review_items; engagementMetrics exposes the automation-ratio KPI. (4) Single Claude wrapper (server/llm/client.ts) with retry/timeout/injectable transport + cost logging to llm_calls, a versioned prompt registry (server/llm/prompts.ts, no inline prompt strings), and an extraction eval harness + CI script (server/llm/evals/) over golden fixtures. (5) Findings engine (server/findings/patterns.ts): pattern interface + registry + the customer_concentration reference pattern + a narrative guard that rejects any drafted number absent from the graph evidence (numbers come from the graph, never the LLM); the other four reference patterns land with the findings slice. zod added (only new dep). No score is ever computed or written here (rule 2); the DRS/ORI engine is untouched and will be wrapped by the score step later. - 2026-07-16 | Verification tab + review-queue API: the advisor-facing surface for document-verified intelligence | Builds the UX that lets an advisor actually drive the sell-side pipeline, plus the review-queue backbone the prompt specified. - 2026-07-17 | Beta test (advisor): fix silent cross-rubric portfolio delta + cover it with tests | Beta-testing the advisor portfolio dashboard surfaced a silent failure: the "Δ since prior" column subtracted the latest and prior DRS scores unconditionally, so when the prior assessment was scored under a different rubric_version the advisor saw a real-looking movement number that is meaningless (the two scores are not on the same scale). This directly violates build-plan S10 ("when the prior assessment is on a different rubric_version, the delta column shows the incomparable state distinctly … never blank or zero") and docs/03's cross-version delta rule. Root cause: the delta was computed inline inside the untestable usePortfolio hook (Supabase-client-bound) with no rubric_version check. Fix: extracted the row assembly into a pure, dependency-free module (src/lib/portfolio.ts, buildPortfolioRows) that only differences scores when latest and prior share a rubric_version; a cross-version prior is reported as deltaState:'incomparable' (delta stays null) and a single-assessment engagement as 'none'. usePortfolio now just fetches and delegates; PortfolioRow moved to and is re-exported from that module. DashboardPage renders the incomparable state as a muted "new rubric" chip (with an explanatory title) instead of a bogus number or a bare em dash, so the advisor can tell "no prior" from "not comparable". Added tests/portfolio.test.ts (+8) covering the same-version numeric delta, one-decimal rounding, the cross-version incomparable guard (the regression), single-assessment 'none', latest/prior selection by sequence_number regardless of input order, open-gap counting, and the missing-company / no-assessment shells. Presentation + pure-logic only — no scoring, schema, or routing change (rule 2 untouched). Full suite 159, tsc -b + vite build clean.
- 2026-07-17 | Buyer-expectations & vendor-DD analysis (docs/15) — proposal only, no rubric/engine change | Analyzed two real diligence artifacts (a live buy-side DD request list for Majic Stairs, a LMM stair/attic-lift manufacturer, and an RIA vendor DD questionnaire for tech vendors) and mapped them against the current DRS rubric + security posture. Central finding: the DRS measures operating quality well (FIN/REV/OPS/CUS/MGT/GRW all validated by the buyer list) but is nearly silent on the transferability/legal-hygiene items that actually retrade or kill LMM deals — three of the buyer's seven sections (Product & IP, Compliance, Legal) sit outside our measurement surface, and they are exactly where this real deal accumulated risk (IP in a founder's name not the company, no written customer/supplier contracts, a settled fraudulent-PPP disclosure, no buy-sell among three equal owners, single-source foreign motor supply). Proposed three work streams for Matthew to decide: (A) new rubric_version extending FIN/OPS with supplier/channel concentration + sales-tax nexus + inventory controls, and adding a Legal & Transferability layer (IP assignment, contract documentation, litigation/regulatory disclosure, insurance, licenses, product liability) — with an open design decision on scored-dimension vs. hard gating-flag (recommend hybrid so a clean operating score can't mask unassigned IP / undisclosed litigation); (B) a deterministic, no-LLM Data Room Readiness surface that ships the buyer's request list back to owners as their pre-built diligence checklist, reusing the R3 documents pipeline and sharing one taxonomy with the gaps; (C) completing ExitBlueprint's own answer to the RIA vendor packet (dogfood) — extends docs/13, closes named gaps (SOC 2 path, BCP/DR, sub-processor register, ≤30-day breach-notification + orderly-termination language, CISO/background-checks/pen-test cadence), and doubles as services/SaaS-segment content. Key v2 moves: (1) new 7th business dimension TRF (Transferability & Legal Readiness, weight 0.10) with 7 sub-scores (IP assignment, contract documentation, corporate/governance, litigation/regulatory, insurance, licenses, environmental) — the hybrid: gradable items scored, binary killers also hard-gated; (2) new signals in existing dimensions — OPS-SUPPLIER (single-source), CUS-CHANNEL (channel concentration), FIN-WORKINGCAP + FIN-TAX, REV-PRICING; (3) de-duplicated customer concentration (removed REV-HHI, kept it in CUS); (4) five hard gating flags (IP_UNASSIGNED, LITIGATION_MATERIAL, REGULATORY_OPEN, ENVIRONMENTAL_CONTAMINATION, TAX_NEXUS_MATERIAL) that cap the tier at Sale Ready per decision 3; (5) rebalanced DRS weights REV .22/FIN .20/OPS .18/CUS .15/MGT .08/GRW .07/TRF .10 (operating dimensions still 0.90). 12 new gap definitions reuse the work-stream-B data-room item codes (one taxonomy, decision 4); industry-specific signals kept in overlays (decision 2). All weight sets validated to sum to 1.00 (per-dimension and effective). No engine/seed/score change — this is a design artifact for Matthew to approve before it becomes a new rubric_version.

- 2026-07-18 | Posture vs vision — database-enforced assessment immutability (docs/23) | Reviewed the vision's (docs/20) load-bearing claims against what the infrastructure actually enforces. Most hold (deterministic scoring is CI-verified vs reference_scorer; multi-tenant RLS is regression-tested; audit trail data_access_log is wired via logAccess). The one gap: "immutable snapshots / defensible evidence / records that withstand institutional diligence" (rule 4) was enforced ONLY by app convention (server/scoring.ts + ledger.ts throw), while the data layer's advisor_firm_all `for all` policy let a client with an advisor JWT UPDATE a finalized drs_score, rewrite its answers, or DELETE the snapshot through PostgREST with no supersede record. Built the guarantee: migration 20260718000200 adds BEFORE UPDATE/DELETE triggers that freeze a completed assessment and its scored children (answers, sub_score_results, dimension_scores). Role-scoped to the untrusted path — the triggers constrain `authenticated`/`anon` (end-user JWT) only; the trusted backend (service_role) and admin/superuser pass through, because corrections are orchestrated server-side as supersede and tenant offboarding/backfills must stay possible. Triggers (not RLS) because they apply to any writer and can express "frozen once completed except via the server path"; scoring is unaffected (INSERTs children while in_progress, flips to completed last). Verified full CI-exact on a fresh DB: test:rls 77 (+6 immutability checks as an authenticated advisor), vitest 202 (DB-integration suites run as superuser, correctly exempt, score→supersede→teardown unaffected), seed/seed:demo ×2 idempotent, eval 8/8, tsc + build clean; plus direct SQL confirming each freeze fires and the supersede bookkeeping update still lands. No scoring/rubric/AI change; app surfaces unchanged. Deferred (recorded): aggregate calibration read, AI institutional reviewer, knowledge-graph materialization.

- 2026-07-19 | Architecture map — visual system overview (docs/28) | Added docs/28-architecture-map.md, a diagram-first companion to the prose in docs/01, so the whole system is graspable at a glance now that the repo is large. - 2026-07-19 | Assessment "Path to 100" — make the whole gap from the current score to 100 legible and route it to remediation (ResultsPage + shared/scoring/interpret + styles.css) | The results page showed the DRS, the six dimension scores, and the fired-gap flags, but never the plain question an advisor and owner actually ask: how far is this from a perfect score, and where are the missing points? Non-negotiable respected — this adds NO new numbers and makes NO scoring decisions: it only re-reads weights/points the engine already produced. The identity (a dimension contributes drsWeight·score and could contribute drsWeight·100, so its recoverable points are drsWeight·(100−score); these sum to exactly 100−DRS) lives in two pure, fixture-adjacent helpers in shared/scoring/interpret.ts — gapToTarget (the whole gap split across the six dimensions, ranked largest-opportunity-first, with each dimension's share of the gap) and subScoreGaps (the measures inside a dimension ranked by the DRS points each would recover to full marks) — so the advisor page and the deterministic owner-report composer can never drift. UI: a gap-summary block (current→100 with a one-line "N points, M of them reach the next tier" caption) over a single composition bar (captured score + one segment per dimension sized to its open points, coloured by status) that shows "all the gaps to 100" at a glance; then the dimension breakdown ranked by recoverable points, each with a "+X open" chip and expanding to its measures showing "+X to DRS" per fix; landing on a remediation CTA that links straight to the engagement roadmap ("Build the remediation roadmap"). - 2026-07-20 | Structural modularity — the six-engine function registry makes the platform-architecture engine model a property of the code (server/registry.ts + functions.ts + entitlements.ts + docs/27/28) | The platform-architecture doc (ExitBlueprintPlatformArchitecture §01) frames the system as six durable engines — Identity, Knowledge, Workflow, Rules, Reasoning, Collaboration — but that taxonomy lived only in prose; the compute router encoded nothing of it, and a function was wired in three drift-prone places (an authorize Set, a dispatch switch case, and its handler) with its engine nowhere in the code. Made the engines structural and inevitable by collapsing the three-place wiring into one declarative table (the "declarative function registry" consolidation candidate recorded in docs/27, now past the ~35-function trigger): server/registry.ts is REGISTRY = { '<name>': { engine, scope, gated?, handler } }, one entry per /functions/v1/* endpoint, grouped by engine. server/functions.ts is now the scope-driven GATEWAY only — handleFunctionCall looks up REGISTRY[name] and authorize() switches on the entry's declared AuthScope (a closed union with an exhaustiveness check, so adding a scope without a gate is a compile error). Security stays explicit and auditable: each scope is one hand-written authorization procedure (firm resolved from the caller's profile, never the body; RLS visibility check) — no dynamic dispatch, no body-shape guessing. Scopes were split finer than the old Sets (document→document-upload/review-queue/document, ledger→ledger-connect/ledger-complete) so each scope is exactly one procedure. entitlements.ts now DERIVES GATED_FNS from the registry's gated flags (single source of truth) instead of a hand-maintained parallel Set. Identity owns zero endpoints on purpose — it IS the gateway (authorize + RLS), documented as such. Behaviour is byte-for-byte unchanged: handleFunctionCall/FunctionContext/FunctionResult public surface preserved, gated set identical (the same 9 paid actions), every authorize branch reproduced. Added tests/registry.test.ts (engine/scope validity, identity-is-the-gateway, GATED_FNS === registry gated set, exactly-the-paid-actions, kebab-case names) and updated docs/27 (pattern §2 rewritten to "add one registry entry"; consolidation marked done) + docs/28 (§6 the six engines + registry, compute-request diagram, module map). - 2026-07-20 | Fix compute-service deploy timeout — decouple the deploy health gate from the DB and bound every DB call (server/http.ts + docs/12) | Render gates the deploy on healthCheckPath /health, and that handler awaited pool.query('select 1') on a pg.Pool created with no connectionTimeoutMillis (pg has no default connect timeout). When the DB was slow/unreachable at deploy time the query hung with no bound, the health request never responded, and Render marked the deploy "Timed Out" → SIGTERM → restart loop (exactly the observed logs: "listening on :10000" then "Timed Out"). Fixed in three parts, all defensive: (1) the pool now sets connectionTimeoutMillis: 10_000 so no DB call can hang forever; (2) /health became a pure LIVENESS probe — it returns 200 {ok:true} if the process is up, with zero external dependency, so a DB blip can never fail the deploy or kill a running instance (a restart loop never fixes a DB outage); (3) added a bounded READINESS probe /ready that does the DB check via a 5s withTimeout race, returning {ok:true,db:true}/200 or {ok:false,db:false}/503 for monitoring / a load balancer, never the deploy gate. Verified with an unreachable DB: /health answers 200 in ~5ms and /ready fails at the 5s bound instead of hanging (previously /health hung indefinitely). docs/12 §3 updated to describe the liveness/readiness split and to point Render at /health, not /ready. No scoring/rubric/schema/RLS/AI change. tsc -b + vite build clean, vitest 152 pass (91 DB-dependent skipped).

- 2026-07-20 | Automatic Clerk provisioning webhook — POST /webhooks/clerk creates firms/advisors/owners on Clerk events (server/clerk-webhook.ts, docs/30 §5) | The admin.ts CLI provisions Clerk but a human has to run it; onboarding needs to be hands-off (end users won't run a CLI). - 2026-07-20 | Compute service must never crash on a DB connection failure — top-level request guard + explicit DATABASE_URL pooler guidance (server/http.ts, render.yaml) | The Clerk webhook was returning 502 in production; Render logs showed the compute service crash-looping on `connect ENETUNREACH 2600:1f18:...:5432` — DATABASE_URL was Supabase's IPv6-only direct connection (db.<ref>.supabase.co:5432), which Render (no outbound IPv6) can't route. Root cause was operational (use the IPv4 session pooler), but the code turned it into an outage: every DB-backed route does `const c = await pool.connect()` OUTSIDE its try/catch, and the createServer callback had no top-level handler, so a rejected connect became an unhandled promise rejection and Node 24 terminated the process (restart loop → 502 on every delivery). Fix: extracted the request body into async handleRequest() and wrapped the createServer callback in `.catch()` that logs and replies 500 when headers aren't sent (else ends the response) — a single bad request or a DB blip now degrades to a clean 5xx (Svix/webhook callers retry; PDF/functions callers get an error) instead of killing the service for everyone. Mirrors the PR #58 principle (a DB blip must not take down the deploy/health path). Also hardened render.yaml's DATABASE_URL comment to name the IPv6/ENETUNREACH trap and require the postgres.<ref>@aws-0-<region>.pooler.supabase.com:5432 session pooler. Verified by running server/http.ts against an unreachable DB and delivering a validly-signed webhook: HTTP 500 returned and the process stayed alive across repeated deliveries (previously the first crashed it). No scoring/rubric/schema/RLS/AI change. tsc (app + node) + vite build clean, vitest 48 pass (6 DB-gated skipped).
- 2026-07-20 | Compute service TLS to the Supabase pooler — control pg ssl in code so the pooler cert doesn't break the connection (server/db-ssl.ts, server/http.ts) | After DATABASE_URL was switched to the Supabase IPv4 pooler (fixing ENETUNREACH), the service then failed with SELF_SIGNED_CERT_IN_CHAIN: the pooler cert chains to Supabase's private CA (not in Node's trust store) and recent pg treats an in-URL sslmode=require as verify-full. Verified against pg that an in-string sslmode overrides an explicit ssl option (client.ssl stays {} = verify), so the fix strips sslmode from the connection string and sets ssl in code. New server/db-ssl.ts resolveDbConnection(url, env): parses + removes sslmode, decides TLS (sslmode wins; else on for a remote host, off for localhost/CI), and returns ssl = {ca, rejectUnauthorized:true} when a CA is supplied (DATABASE_CA_CERT inline PEM or PGSSLROOTCERT path) else {rejectUnauthorized:false} (encrypted, unverified). server/http.ts builds the pool from the stripped connectionString + resolved ssl and warns in production when TLS is unverified (mirrors the EB_DOCUMENT_KEY nudge). Local dev/CI (no sslmode, localhost) get ssl:false — plain, unchanged. Documented DATABASE_CA_CERT in .env.example + render.yaml. Added tests/db-ssl.test.ts (6 pure cases: sslmode stripped, remote-unverified, CA-verified, local-plain, sslmode=disable, remote-default-on). Verified by booting server/http.ts with a sslmode=require pooler URL: it starts, logs the unverified-TLS warning, /health 200, no more verify-full alias warning (sslmode stripped). No scoring/rubric/schema/RLS/AI change. tsc (app + node) + vite build clean, vitest 48 pass (6 DB-gated skipped) + 6 new db-ssl.
- 2026-07-20 | Profile gate tolerates provisioning lag — retry the profile lookup before showing the "not set up" state (src/lib/auth.tsx, src/App.tsx) | With automatic Clerk-webhook provisioning, a brand-new user's profile row is written a beat AFTER first sign-in, and the Clerk→supabase access token needs a moment to attach (an unauthenticated read returns 0 rows under RLS). The single-shot useProfile lookup therefore missed and RequireAdvisor/RequireStaff flashed a terminal "This account has no advisor profile. Provision one with scripts/admin.ts." until a manual browser refresh re-queried. Fixed useProfile to retry the profiles read with backoff (attempts at 0/0.5/1/2/3.5s ≈ 7s total) and stop on the first hit — zero added latency for existing users (first attempt has no delay and breaks immediately), so only a missing profile waits. During the retry profileLoading stays true, so the gates show "Loading…" rather than the error, and the workspace renders as soon as the row lands. Also replaced the two developer-facing terminal messages (which told an end user to run a CLI — wrong now that provisioning is automatic) with a shared ProfileNotReady component: a plain-language "Your account isn't set up yet… give it a moment and refresh / contact your administrator" plus a Refresh button. - 2026-07-20 | Production go-live debug — structured loading/error UI system + Clerk↔Supabase auth diagnostic (src/lib/errors.ts, src/components/ui/{LoadingState,ErrorState,AsyncBoundary}, HealthPage, docs/26 §Loading & error states, docs/31) | First live session on app.exitblueprint.net surfaced two things: pervasive "database errors", and loading/error messages rendered as bare unstyled text. That's dashboard config, not code (accessToken:()=>getToken() is already correct), so shipped diagnosis + hardening rather than a code "fix": (1) DIAGNOSTIC — /health now decodes the live session token and checks sub/issuer, `role: authenticated` (the decisive check, with the docs/31 fix pointer when missing), expiry, and an end-to-end authenticated read of the methodology tables; getAccessToken() exported from supabase.ts to support it. (2) NOISE — src/lib/auth.tsx profile/firm lookups .single()→.maybeSingle(): .single() 406s on 0 rows and the first-sign-in provisioning retry loop fired up to 5, spraying red DB errors in the console every fresh login. (3) UI SYSTEM (the explicit ask) — new LoadingState (page/section/inline), ErrorState (runs thrown values through describeError() which humanizes Supabase/PostgREST/network errors and adds the auth-config hint for RLS-shaped failures; page/section/inline), and AsyncBoundary (maps a TanStack Query result to loading→error→empty→content with retry=refetch). Replaced the App.tsx route-gate `<p className="muted page">Loading…</p>`, ProfileNotReady, and ~18 page-level `<p className="form-error">{raw}</p>` / plain-loading sites across the workspace; kept `.form-error` only for short field-level validation hints and the static "auth not configured" panel. - 2026-07-20 | Admins are firm staff in the workspace — grant role='admin' the same firm-scoped RLS as advisors (supabase/migrations/20260720000100_admin_firm_access.sql, scripts/rls-test.ts, docs/31) | Live debugging of the app.exitblueprint.net "database errors" ended here: /health's new Profile linkage check showed the signed-in account had a correctly-keyed profile with role `admin`, and Firm-scoped read returned 0. Root cause: the frontend admits role='admin' to the advisor/staff surfaces (App.tsx RequireAdvisor/RequireStaff both allow admin), but every firm-scoped RLS policy gated on 'advisor' (or 'advisor'/'reviewer') only — the base RLS file even documented "admin: server-side only via service_role; no admin policies here" — so an admin signed in through the browser could read/write NOTHING firm-scoped (0-row reads, denied writes) → pervasive "database errors". Matthew chose to make admin a first-class firm-staff role for data access (matching what the frontend already assumes) rather than restrict provisioning. Implemented ADDITIVELY to eliminate regression risk: a new migration adds permissive admin_* policies alongside the existing advisor/staff policies (Postgres ORs permissive policies per command), so not one existing policy body changes and advisor/reviewer/owner access is byte-for-byte identical. Each admin policy MIRRORS the command and scoping of the advisor/staff policy it shadows — `for all` where staff have full access (30 firm_id-scoped tables + the 3 assessment-scoped child tables answers/sub_score_results/dimension_scores via the same exists() shape), SELECT-only on the audit/usage/billing tables staff only read (data_access_log/firm_subscriptions/llm_calls/usage_events), profiles firm read, agreement_versions insert, outcome_events append-only (select+insert) — all still gated on firm_id = app.user_firm_id(), so firm isolation is preserved. profiles.role stays the RLS source of truth; admin remains org:admin in Clerk for org management. Verified by applying the migration to a FRESH db and running rls-test: 87/87 pass (80 prior + 7 new admin checks proving full firm-A access AND zero firm-B read/write). No scoring/rubric/schema-shape/AI change; no existing RLS policy modified. tsc -b + vite build clean, vitest 176 pass.

- 2026-07-20 | Continuous-evaluation webhooks (server/scheduled.ts, POST /webhooks/scheduled/{stale-engagements,stalled-tasks,reassessment-due}) | Realized the architecture doc §07 mechanism this repo was specced to expose: authenticated endpoints an external n8n instance calls on a schedule to ask "what changed / went quiet?" instead of waiting on a calendar. Three read-only, cross-firm (service-role) analyzers returning a uniform { generatedAt, thresholdDays, count, items[] } with firm_id per item for per-firm routing — stale engagements (no assessment/log activity in N=30d), stalled tasks (open + untouched N=14d or past due), reassessment due (last completed assessment older than N=90d). Read-only by construction: never writes a score, never mutates an immutable assessment (rules 4 & 5) — it surfaces that a re-assessment is due, it doesn't create one. Auth is a shared secret (x-webhook-secret vs WEBHOOK_SECRET) via a constant-time verifyWebhookSecret (length-guarded timingSafeEqual), NOT a user JWT — n8n is a trusted system caller like scripts/admin.ts. Query strings + row→item mappers exported pure for DB-free unit testing. tasks/engagements have no updated_at, so "untouched" is measured from created_at (documented). Wired in http.ts (503 when WEBHOOK_SECRET unset). Env: WEBHOOK_SECRET (render.yaml + .env.example). Tests: tests/scheduled.test.ts 15. No migration, no new table (stateless analyzers).

- 2026-07-20 | Fix "we couldn't reach the server" across function-backed views — CORS allowlist was emitted as an invalid header + a coding TypeError was mislabeled as an outage (server/cors.ts, server/http.ts, src/lib/errors.ts) | Prod reported a blanket "we couldn't reach the server" in multiple places. Root cause: server/http.ts documented FUNCTIONS_ALLOWED_ORIGIN as a comma-separated allowlist but set the raw env string verbatim as Access-Control-Allow-Origin — a header that may only be a single origin or '*', never a comma-joined list. So the moment prod tightened CORS to more than one origin (apex + www), every browser rejected the preflight and all function calls (explain/valuation/comparables/verification/education/advisory/cim-coverage/compare — the core assessment+report views) failed as fetch TypeErrors, while plain Supabase REST reads still worked. Fix: extracted a pure server/cors.ts (parseAllowedOrigins + resolveCorsOrigin) that parses the list and echoes back the request's own Origin when it's allowlisted (falls back to the first configured origin for a non-listed/missing Origin, adds Vary: Origin), wired into setCors(req,res). Second, honesty fix: describeError treated ANY TypeError as network ("check your connection"), so a plain coding TypeError (e.g. "Cannot read properties of undefined") was disguised as a server outage; narrowed it to match the recognizable fetch-failure messages (Chrome/Firefox/Safari/undici) so real bugs surface instead of hiding. No scoring/rubric/immutable-assessment/RLS/AI change. Tests: tests/cors.test.ts 6 (default-any, comma split, per-request echo, non-listed fallback, never comma-joined) + tests/errors.test.ts extended (all-browser fetch messages → network; coding TypeError → not network). tsc (app + node) clean, vitest 230 pass.

- 2026-07-20 | CLM completeness: engagement lifecycle management + hard delete (server/engagements.ts, registry `delete-engagement` + `delete-engagement` auth scope, EngagementPage Setup & admin, ConfirmDialog `confirmDisabled`) | The engagement was creatable and readable but never manageable: its status (active|paused|exited|churned) was display-only with no control, and there was no way to remove one — a mis-created engagement or a client "delete our data" request had no path. Added the soft path (a Status control on the Setup & admin tab; a plain firm-scoped UPDATE under the existing advisor RLS) and the destructive path (a real hard delete, not an archive). Hard delete MUST be a service-role function: an engagement is the root of a deep tree whose FKs are deliberately not ON DELETE CASCADE (nothing but this teardown may remove client history), and the immutability triggers (#20260718000200) plus append-only grants (outcome_events, llm_calls, data_access_log) mean an advisor JWT running as `authenticated` cannot tear it down — the completed-assessment freeze exempts only service_role/maintenance roles, which is exactly why it lives server-side. deleteEngagement() runs one transaction of FK-safe ordered deletes across every engagement-child table (sell-side graph, documents+blobs, valuation, data room, outcomes, roadmap/log/instrumentation, the assessment sub-tree, agreement), then a DYNAMIC orphan check (information_schema for any public table with an engagement_id column still holding rows) so a future table added without updating the teardown fails loudly and rolls back rather than orphaning data; the removal is audited into data_access_log with engagement_id null + ids in detail so the record survives its own subject. Scope `delete-engagement` restricts it to advisor/admin (owners/reviewers can see an engagement but must not delete it) and is deliberately un-gated (removing data must never be blocked by a lapsed subscription). UI gates it behind a harsh, type-the-client-name confirmation that itemizes exactly what will be destroyed (assessments+score history, gaps, tasks, documents, valuation, the un-re-derivable deal-outcome calibration record, …). No scoring/rubric/immutable-assessment/RLS-policy change. Tests: tests/functions.test.ts builds an engagement loaded with the tricky-ordering children (gap→assessment, task+milestone→gap, deal_outcome→assessment, doc+blob, append-only outcome_events) and asserts one call empties every table + writes the audit row, plus advisor/admin-only (403) and foreign-engagement (404) denials. - 2026-07-20 | Auth session-lifecycle UX pass — recover from mid-session expiry, warn before idle logout, return to intent after login, theme the Clerk widget (src/lib/sessionExpiry.ts, src/lib/auth.tsx, src/App.tsx, src/components/ui/{ErrorState,AsyncBoundary,IdleWarningModal}.tsx, src/pages/LoginPage.tsx) | The auth seam handled cold-load well (spinner-before-session, maybeSingle profile backoff) but dropped off after the happy path — the "clunk" on the identity boundary. Four fixes, all extending existing patterns. (1) Mid-session expiry recovery: errors.ts already classified a stale/invalid JWT as kind:'auth' but nothing acted on it — the QueryClient had no onError, and AsyncBoundary wired a refetch "Try again" that re-failed with the dead token (a retry-of-death). Added a QueryCache onError that runs describeError and, on kind:'auth', calls notifySessionExpired() (new src/lib/sessionExpiry.ts — a React-free bridge the module-level QueryClient uses to reach the AuthProvider, re-entrancy-guarded so a storm of failing queries yields one sign-out). Both providers register a handler that signs out; the gates then route to /login. AsyncBoundary now only wires the refetch retry when describeError().retryable, and ErrorState renders a real "Sign in again" action (→ notifySessionExpired) for kind:'auth' instead of a dead card. (2) Idle logout was silent — useIdleTimeout signed out at 30min with no notice; refactored to two-phase (warn 60s before with a live countdown via new IdleWarningModal reusing the .ui-modal surface; any activity or "Stay signed in" resets), and /login now explains why via a one-shot sessionStorage reason (idle vs expired). (3) Deep-link return: gates already stashed location.state.from but LoginPage discarded it — now reads it into returnTo and passes it to navigate() (dev) and Clerk <SignIn forceRedirectUrl> (prod). (4) Clerk <SignIn> ignored the app theme — added appearance built from the app's own CSS tokens (read via getComputedStyle, recomputed on theme change) so the widget matches chrome in light/dark. Guarded a StrictMode pitfall: the signout-reason read is a pure peek during render + a cancellable clear in an effect, so the dev double-mount doesn't wipe the notice (would have misfired in prod too). No scoring/rubric/immutable-assessment/RLS/AI change. Tests: new tests/sessionExpiry.test.ts (handler dispatch, storm-collapse + re-arm, one-shot reason); tsc clean, vitest 234 pass, build green; login notice + Clerk theming driven live in a browser (dark/light).

- 2026-07-20 | Roadmap reorder correctness — dedicated tasks.display_order (migration 20260720000300, src/lib/queries.ts TaskRow, src/pages/RoadmapPage.tsx) | The first cut of the roadmap reorder swapped tasks.sequence, which is wrong: `sequence` is the per-playbook template position and forms the idempotency key (playbook_id:sequence) server/roadmap.ts uses to skip already-generated tasks, so a swap would (a) no-op whenever two adjacent tasks shared a sequence value — sequences repeat across playbooks — and (b) on the next reschedule make generation re-insert duplicate tasks. - 2026-07-20 | R5 secure document storage — Supabase Storage backend + real virus scanning behind opt-in env seams (server/documents/storage.ts, scanner.ts, pipeline.ts, engagements.ts, migration 20260720000600, DocumentsPage.tsx) | The docs pipeline's two deferred "R5 follow-up" stubs were the object-storage backend and the virus scan; encryption-at-rest, HMAC signed URLs, RLS, MFA, and the audit log had already shipped. Implemented both without touching any caller, defaults unchanged (db/noop) so CI and the dev emulator stay byte-identical. (1) StorageAdapter gained a SupabaseStorage backend (EB_STORAGE=supabase, lazy service-role client from SUPABASE_URL + SUPABASE_SERVICE_ROLE_KEY + EB_STORAGE_BUCKET): the SAME AES-256-GCM envelope we already store is uploaded as ciphertext to a private bucket keyed firm_id/document_id — deliberately keeping app-layer encryption + serve-through-our-function over Supabase's native at-rest + native signed URLs, because key custody stays in EB_DOCUMENT_KEY (a leaked object URL yields only ciphertext) and every read stays on the route that writes data_access_log (native signed URLs would bypass the audit trail). Trade-off accepted: bytes transit compute (fine at the 15 MB cap). (2) A ScannerAdapter seam (mirroring ParserAdapter, no npm dep) with NoopScanner (default, records scan_status='skipped'), a raw-clamd-INSTREAM ClamAVScanner (EB_SCANNER=clamav, fail-CLOSED on an unreachable daemon — never silently accept), and a FixtureScanner test seam (eicar→infected). (3) uploadDocument reordered to scan the plaintext BEFORE storage.put, so an infected file is recorded scan_status='infected' + status='rejected' and NEVER persisted (no malware object to clean up); a server-side extension allow-list (pdf/csv/txt/xls/xlsx/doc/docx/png/jpg/jpeg) sits by the size cap; a best-effort storage.remove compensates a bucket write a later txn failure can't roll back. (4) StorageAdapter.remove(db,{documentId,firmId}) added (path derived deterministically, since the documents row is already gone when it runs) and wired into deleteEngagement (snapshot doc ids pre-teardown, remove objects post-commit) — a bucket object does not cascade like document_blobs does. (5) Guarded migration 20260720000600 creates the private bucket only when the storage schema exists (no-op on the plain-Postgres shim). Frontend: client-side allow-list + size check before base64, an accept filter, a rejected-upload toast, and an "Infected" chip. No scoring/rubric/immutable-assessment change (rules 1–6 intact) — this is storage + scan hardening over the existing pipeline. Live Supabase-Storage/clamd verification is an ops step (needs a real bucket/daemon); offline the FixtureScanner exercises the full infected→rejected branch and defaults keep every existing test green.

- 2026-07-21 | Fixture parser tolerates non-JSON source documents (server/documents/parser.ts) | Fixes a `seed:demo` idempotency regression from the file-driven-intake slice (#97): seed-demo attaches P&L / revenue-by-customer CSVs to the demo engagement *after* the fixture-parser verification run, so the first run is fine, but the CSVs persist and the second (idempotency) run feeds them to the sell-side pipeline's parse step (server/pipeline/steps.ts runs every non-rejected document through the active parser), where FixtureParserAdapter did `JSON.parse` and threw "document bytes are not valid JSON", failing the whole seed and turning CI red on main. An engagement can now legitimately hold non-fixture source files, so the fixture adapter treats a non-JSON document as a no-op ("nothing to extract", the same as the manual adapter) instead of aborting the run — but a document that CLAIMS to be JSON (application/json mime or .json extension) yet doesn't parse still throws, so a broken golden-test fixture fails loudly as before. Production is unaffected (EB_PARSER unset → manual adapter, which never throws); this only bites the fixture path used by seed-demo and the sell-side golden test. No scoring/rubric/immutable-assessment/RLS/AI change (rules 1–6 intact). Verified on fresh Postgres 16: migrate → seed → seed:demo ×2 both green (idempotent) → vitest 400 pass (incl. sellside-pipeline + pl-extract) → tsc -b + vite build clean.

- 2026-07-21 | Reconciliation rigor — wire the self-reported side + numeric tolerance + broadened field map (System B) | First landed slice of a larger document-ingestion / financial-verification hardening effort. The document-verification reconciliation pipeline was effectively theater: the self-reported side was never passed into the job (server/sellside.ts createJob omitted selfReported), so hasSelf was always false and every field auto-resolved to document_verified; and the conflict test was raw `String(a) !== String(b)` (no tolerance). Fixed, deterministic and rule-1/2 safe (reconciliation writes only assessment_values/findings/review_items — never a score, never an `answers` row, no LLM): (1) sellside.ts loads the engagement's current-assessment answers for the mapped fields (read-only direct query, since scoring.ts loadAnswers is not exported) and passes them as the job's selfReported checkpoint, so reconcile performs a genuine self-vs-verified comparison. (2) field-map.ts gains a typed FieldMapping and a numeric tolerance band — `compareValues` returns match / within_tolerance / conflict, agreeing when values differ by no more than max($1 absolute, 1% relative) after unit normalization (normalizeNumeric strips $/,/% and treats (x) as negative); non-numeric fields fall back to a normalized string compare so e.g. "unknown" vs "unknown" no longer spuriously conflicts. Only a genuine `conflict` queues a conflict review item. (3) ASSESSMENT_FIELD_MAP broadened from 2 to 5 mapped facts (revenue, ebitda, recurring-% , NRR, industry), each annotated as scored vs extractable-only; `selectSelfValue` reduces a numeric_list answer (e.g. REV-ANNUAL's four-year series) to the scalar the singleton fact represents. New tests/reconciliation-compare.test.ts (13 pure-logic cases) locks the tolerance/normalization behavior. The rest of the hardening scope (document-ingestion security P0s — status guard, scan-clean gate, prod key boot-guards, force-attachment/magic-byte/filename; and financial-evidence — an evidence FK on answer_provenance requiring a stored document for 'document'-verified, P&L totals validation, verification audit trail) was drafted by parallel agents but reverted unshipped: the agents were cut off mid-edit by a session limit, leaving the evidence migration CI-breaking (its CHECK conflicts with seed/rls-test rows that stamp source='document' without evidence) and its enforcement code unwritten, and the ingestion changes half-wired. Those remain deferred to a fresh, complete pass; the weakness map from the recon stands as the spec. Verified: tsc -b clean, vitest 302 passed.

- 2026-07-21 | Document-ingestion & financial-verification hardening — security P0s + evidence-backed provenance (no scoring touched) | The ingestion pipeline and financial "verification" were weak (see the recon weakness-map). Hardened both as deterministic overlays; no LLM, no score/answers mutation (rules 1/2). Migrations are ADDITIVE-ONLY with NO retroactive hard CHECK — the last attempt broke CI because a `source='document' → evidence not null` CHECK conflicted with existing seed/rls-test/verification inserts; the invariant is enforced in application code (the only path that stamps 'document' in production) instead. **Document ingestion** (server/documents/pipeline.ts, server/http.ts, ReviewDocumentPage, migration 20260722000300): (1) status guard — only an in_review doc may be verified; (2) require-confirmed-fields — verify is blocked while any document_fields row is still verification_status='extracted' (zero-field docs still verify); (3) scan gate — store/extract/serve requires scan_status='clean', with 'skipped' allowed only when NODE_ENV!=='production'; (4) prod boot-guards — missing EB_DOCUMENT_KEY or EB_SIGNING_KEY hard-fails startup in production (closes the forgeable-signed-URL fallback); (5) safe serve — download forces Content-Disposition: attachment for non-image/pdf, recomputes content-type from the sanitized extension, adds nosniff, and the review preview sandboxes the iframe (fixes stored-XSS via browser MIME); (6) magic-byte sniff using positive-mismatch detection (reject only when bytes match a DIFFERENT known signature, so signatureless text/CSV always pass — required for the data-room CI uploads); (7) filename sanitization; (8) content_sha256 + per-engagement dedup; (9) document_fields.confidence CHECK [0,1]. **Financial verification** (server/ledger.ts, pl-extract.ts, audit.ts, verification.ts, PLImportPanel, AccountingCard, queries.ts, migration 20260722000400): evidence link — nullable evidence_document_id/evidence_fact_id on answer_provenance; enterManualFinancials now requires a resolvable same-firm evidence_document_id to stamp 'document' and otherwise DOWNGRADES to self_reported, so "document-verified" can no longer mean "a number the parser liked with the file discarded"; PLImportPanel now persists the uploaded P&L via upload-document and passes its id as the evidence; deterministic P&L validation (validateRevenueSeries/validateShares — sign/magnitude/units/period-jump/cross-foot checks that flag but never adjust a figure, downgrading flagged figures to self_reported); an append-only answer_provenance_events audit table (immutable — select/insert only; advisor firm-scoped + owner company-scoped RLS mirroring 20260713000100) written on every provenance mutation via logProvenanceEvent, plus logAccess records; honest connected-ledger labeling ("automatic import not yet enabled") since the provider pull is still phase-3. ledger.test.ts updated to supply/deny evidence and assert the downgrade; new pure tests document-integrity.test.ts (11) + provenance-evidence.test.ts (12). Still deferred: real ledger data-pull (external/phase-3), a defense-in-depth DB CHECK on provenance evidence (needs all fixtures to carry evidence first), and unifying the two verification systems / populating the raw-vs-verified scores table. Verified: tsc -b clean, vitest 325 passed (DB-integration suites run in CI).

- 2026-07-21 | Mobile/UI styling fixes: theme-toggle glyph, tiling select chevron, shadowed table headers, defensive grid collapse (src/lib/theme.tsx, src/styles.css) | Four reported presentation bugs, CSS/markup only — no scoring/rubric/immutable-assessment/RLS/AI change (rules 1–6 intact). (1) THEME TOGGLE showed a color emoji on mobile: the ☀/☾ unicode chars get promoted to emoji presentation by mobile browsers. Replaced with inline monochrome SVG sun/moon icons (currentColor, so they inherit the button's themed text color in light+dark). (2) "DROPDOWNS COVERED IN ARROWS": the select chevron tiled across the whole control in dark theme on the Library filters (.advisory-filters), advisory form, and plan rows. Root cause: those per-surface rules set the `background` SHORTHAND (background: var(--surface-*)), which resets background-repeat→repeat and background-position→0 0; the higher-specificity :root[data-theme='dark'] select override then re-added only the chevron IMAGE, so it repeated from top-left. Fixed by switching those four rules to `background-color` (preserves the base select's chevron/no-repeat/position — also restores the chevron that the shorthand was silently killing in light theme), and hardened the two dark-theme select overrides to re-assert background-repeat:no-repeat + position so a future shorthand can't reintroduce the tiling. (3) "COLUMNS WEIRDLY SHADOWED": sortable table headers (.ui-table-sort) rendered a faint raised-button gradient box while non-sortable headers stayed flat. The text-button reset (background-image:none) was out-specificity'd by the later button:not(.btn-secondary):not(.btn-ghost):not(.linkish) gradient rule; added .ui-table-sort/.comparison-toggle/.advisory-item-toggle/.button-danger-link/.learn-head to that rule's :not() exclusions. (4) ORGANIZATION/BRANDING form-field spill: could not reproduce a page-level horizontal overflow on the live page at 320/360/390px (the .settings-grid/.team-invite-row collapse already handles it), but hardened the mobile collapse from bare `1fr` to `minmax(0,1fr)` so a wide child can't blow the track past the viewport. Verified live in the seeded demo (Playwright): Library filters show one clean chevron in both themes, dashboard table headers are flat, theme toggle renders the SVG, and Organization has scrollWidth==viewport at 320/360/390. tsc -b + vite build clean, vitest 289 pass / 144 skipped.
