Three product decisions (Matthew): (1) **Add a plan** is a first-class picker on the roadmap (active system+firm Plans not already applied), applying with the shared anchor date and a soft "Remove plan" that keeps client task history (status='removed'; its rows fall back to the unplanned bucket). (2) `recommend-plans` now fires from **two** deterministic signals — a Plan's playbook items targeting open gaps (as before) AND its advisory items referencing a **fired initiative** (advisory.ts, item_type='initiative', reused verbatim), ranked by combined coverage (match_score = gaps + initiatives); read-only over scoring/gaps (rules 1 & 4). (3) `generate-roadmap` **auto-applies** any Plan that is *substantively applicable* — a MAJORITY (≥50%) of its playbook items map to the engagement's open gaps — reusing applyPlan's once-per-engagement (playbook_id, sequence) idempotency so a claimed task is never doubled, and reports what it applied in the toast ("apply + report"). Stricter than the single-match recommendation arm so bulk generation only pulls in mostly-on-target Plans. No scoring/rubric/schema change (additive TS interface fields only) and no LLM in any path. Verified against a real Postgres: migrations + seed (×2) clean, RLS 122/0, full vitest 446/446 (the 3 new plans cases run), tsc -b + vite build clean.

- 2026-07-21 | Bug sweep: PostgREST schema-cache reload on migrate + five UI fixes (scripts/migrate.ts, src/lib/format.ts, src/styles.css) | Reported bugs, no scoring/rubric/immutable-assessment/RLS/AI change (rules 1–6 intact). (1) COMMENTS "Could not find the table 'public.engagement_comments' in the schema cache": migrations are applied over a raw pg connection (scripts/migrate.ts), not the Supabase CLI, so on a hosted project PostgREST never learns about newly created tables and REST calls 404 on them. migrate() now issues `notify pgrst, 'reload schema'` after every run (outside the apply loop, so re-running `db:migrate` fixes an already-stale cache even with nothing new to apply; a harmless no-op on plain Postgres). (2) CIM CASING everywhere: the shared `humanizeKey` humanizer had no entry for `cim`, so `doc_type='cim'` rendered as "Cim" (e.g. the assessment/document record rows on EngagementPage). Added `cim`/`drs`/`ori`/`nda`/`loi` to the ACRONYMS map so every humanized surface cases them correctly. (3) ROADMAP PLAN BUTTONS "weird shading": the `.rm-group-toggle` disclosure button (the Plan group title under Plans & work) wasn't in the text-button exclusion list, so it picked up the raised-box `button` box-shadow + gradient background-image and read as a faint shadowed box — the exact failure mode the neighboring comment describes. Added it to the gradient `:not()` chain and the box-shadow/background-image reset, matching the prior `.ui-table-sort` fix. (4) BUYER LENS "Preparation" spacing: `.advisory-detail-label` was an inline span glued to its paragraph (0.15rem gap); made it `display:block` with margin-bottom so the eyebrow label sits cleanly above its text (also improves the same label in Library/Plans). (5) ANALYSIS & DETAIL tabs off-screen on mobile: `.subtabs` is `inline-flex`, which grows to content width and overflows the viewport rather than scrolling; the mobile rule now forces `display:flex; max-width:100%` so `overflow-x:auto` actually clips + scrolls the strip. Verified: tsc -b + vite build clean, vitest 336 pass / 148 skipped.
- 2026-07-21 | White-labeling fix: one firm accent now rebrands primary buttons (bg + hover) and brand focus rings, not just links (src/lib/color.ts, src/lib/branding.tsx, src/styles.css, src/pages/OrganizationPage.tsx, tests/color.test.ts) | Reported bug: setting a firm accent color changed links/accents but NOT most button colors. Root cause: BrandingProvider only overrode --accent, while the primary button used a SEPARATE hardcoded variable set (--btn-bg/--btn-bg-hover/--btn-fg = forest literals unrelated to --accent), so an accent override never reached buttons. Fix routes the derivation through the provider rather than the naive CSS refactor: a new dependency-free pure helper (src/lib/color.ts) parses a hex (#rgb/#rrggbb), darkens by a fixed 20% for the -strong/hover shade, and picks a WCAG-readable on-accent foreground (white vs near-black by contrast); accentVars(hex) returns the coherent set {--accent, --accent-strong, --btn-bg, --btn-bg-hover, --btn-fg} or null for invalid input (→ keep defaults). BrandingProvider now applies that whole set to the client-facing subtree wrapper (was --accent only); links, focus rings and .btn all already read these tokens so ONE value rebrands them in both light and dark. Deliberately did NOT make the CSS default --btn-bg:var(--accent): the dark-theme default accent (#4bb888) is a bright tint that only reaches 2.47:1 with white text (fails AA) and would also visibly change the unbranded dark button — so the per-theme button literals stay as the default (byte-identical, AA in both themes) and branding overrides them with a luminance-picked foreground (best-effort AA for user-chosen colors, AA guaranteed for the default). Org branding live preview now uses accentVars so its sample button reflects the real coherent behavior. Tier/chart colors untouched (fixed ordinal palette, tokens.ts JS tier colors unchanged). No scoring/rubric/immutable-assessment/RLS/AI change (rules 1-6 intact) — CSS/branding presentation only. Verified: tsc -b + vite build clean; vitest 344 pass / 148 skipped incl. 8 new color-helper cases (parse/darken/readable-AA/accentVars). test:rls not run — no local Postgres/Docker in this sandbox; change touches no schema/RLS/firm_id so isolation is unaffected.

- 2026-07-22 | Fix failing Render deploys — declare EB_SIGNING_KEY in render.yaml | Commit 50accc8 added a production hard-fail in `server/http.ts` requiring `EB_SIGNING_KEY` (so document download-token HMAC never falls back to the public dev key), but `render.yaml` was never updated to provide it. With `NODE_ENV=production` set in `server/Dockerfile`, the container `process.exit(1)`ed at startup, so `/health` never came up and every Render deploy failed the health-check gate. Added `EB_SIGNING_KEY` to the blueprint with `generateValue: true` (vs EB_DOCUMENT_KEY's `sync: false`): it signs only ephemeral 5-min download tokens, so Render can auto-generate a strong value with no manual dashboard step and the deploy self-heals. Verified: prod-mode startup now serves `/health` 200 with the key present, exits 1 without it.

the enum value lingers, un-droppable), `gap_plan_map` replacing `gap_playbook_map` (a gap links to its remediation **Plan** — the "roadmap initiative"), `tasks.library_task_id` replacing `tasks.playbook_id` as the once-per-engagement idempotency key, and `playbooks`/`playbook_task_templates`/`gap_playbook_map` dropped. **Engine**: the two instantiation copies merged into one — `applyPlan` (server/plans.ts) is now the SOLE path that lays tasks onto the roadmap; - 2026-07-22 | Outcome Calibration Engine (the "FICO moat", docs/09 §1, docs/40 §3) — a versioned, deterministic DRS/ORI-band calibration artifact over the cross-firm deal_outcomes corpus | The platform captured paired prediction↔reality records (deal_outcomes) and thin one-row moat KPIs (server/moat-metrics.ts, analytics.calibration_corpus), but never turned the corpus into a *calibrated* read of the score. Added a rule-based calibration layer that buckets outcomes by DRS (and ORI) score band and reports, per band, {sample_n, closed_n, close_rate, median + interquartile realized multiple, median time-to-close, within-range hit rate, EV variance, retrade rate, contributing_firms} — e.g. "companies at DRS 70–75 close at ~4.8× within ~14 months, 82% of the time." **Pure math** `shared/calibration/compute.ts` (deterministic, no LLM, no I/O — rule #1; DRS/ORI never mixed — rule #3a), unit-tested fixture-style in `tests/calibration.test.ts` (bucketing, top-band fold, close rate, median/IQR multiple, within-range, EV variance, retrade, group separation, low-confidence/de-identification guard, determinism, empty corpus, plus the readCalibration fake-db shape and the calibrationBands helper). **Server** `server/calibration.ts`: computeCalibration reads the cross-firm corpus on the service-role connection and PERSISTS a new immutable `calibration_version` snapshot; readCalibration returns the latest — registered as `compute-calibration` + `read-calibration` (Rules Engine, `platform-admin` scope) in server/registry.ts and wired into the superadmin `GET /internal/metrics` rail (server/http.ts) as a new `calibration` block, mirroring moat-metrics/financial-corpus. **Migration** `20260722214544_calibration_engine.sql` adds `analytics.calibration_versions` + `analytics.calibration_bands` + `analytics.calibration_latest` in the walled, service-role-only `analytics` schema — CROSS-FIRM aggregate intelligence behind the superadmin path, de-identified (no firm_id/PII; a band's contributing_firms<2 or thin sample flags low_confidence), never a firm-facing cross-firm read (rule #5). Calibration NEVER edits a live score — it appends a versioned artifact that would inform the rubric only via a future rubric_version (rules #1, #3, #4); assessments stay immutable. **Readout**: a new "DRS calibration" SectionCard on the superadmin PlatformConsolePage (design-system tables per docs/26), added WITHOUT disturbing the operating-dashboard `operating` block/sections. - 2026-07-22 | Fix "Could not find the table 'public.library_tasks' in the schema cache" — self-service methodology load now reloads the PostgREST schema cache | The playbooks→Plans unification (#129) introduced brand-new tables (`library_tasks`, `gap_plan_map`) that PostgREST must learn about before the app's REST reads of them succeed. The reload signal (`notify pgrst, 'reload schema'`) lived ONLY in `scripts/migrate.ts` (added #122), but production loads methodology through the in-system, superadmin-gated `seed-methodology` function ("Load methodology" on `/health`) precisely so nobody runs the CLI against a production connection string — and migrations there are applied out-of-band (Supabase CLI/dashboard), so the migrate.ts reload never fires and PostgREST keeps serving a stale cache that 404s the new tables. Fix: `writeSeedBundle` (`server/seed-methodology.ts`) now issues `notify pgrst, 'reload schema'` over the service-role connection right after the write completes, closing the gap through the same self-service path the methodology loader is designed around. Best-effort (`.catch(() => {})`) so a cache hiccup can't discard an otherwise-successful seed report; harmless no-op on plain Postgres (no listener) and in CI. No scoring/rubric/schema/migration/RLS/AI change (rules 1–6 intact). Verified: `npm run build` clean, `npm test` 355 passed / 148 skipped.
- 2026-07-22 | "Load methodology" now applies pending migrations before seeding — schema-changing methodology updates land in-system without CLI access to prod | Follow-up to #130. - 2026-07-22 | Fix "Load methodology" migrate step colliding on an already-provisioned DB (`type "firm_status" already exists`) — reconcile the Supabase CLI migration ledger, never re-run applied migrations | Follow-up to #131. On the hosted DB, "Load methodology" (`seed-methodology` → `applyMigrations`, server/migrate.ts) found OUR ledger `public.schema_migrations` empty and replayed history from the first migration, colliding with objects already created out-of-band. A hosted Supabase project is provisioned by the Supabase CLI (`supabase db push`), which records applied migrations in `supabase_migrations.schema_migrations` keyed by the 14-digit VERSION (the filename's timestamp prefix), NOT in our table. Key finding: **re-running an applied migration is unsafe two ways** — the first CREATE collides ("already exists"), and even if that were swallowed, an old migration re-run against a schema that LATER migrations have since evolved fails semantically (proved locally: `20260707000200_rls.sql` re-run → `operator does not exist: text = uuid`, a policy comparing a column a later migration retyped). So the applied set must be determined WITHOUT executing. Fix: `applyMigrations` now treats a file as applied if our ledger has its filename OR the CLI ledger has its version; applied-but-unrecorded files are **baselined** (recorded in our ledger, never run) and only genuinely-new files run. If a collision still occurs (a DB provisioned via the dashboard SQL editor, tracked by neither ledger), it now throws an actionable "baseline it once, then retry" error instead of a cryptic first-collision. Verified locally against a simulated `db push` DB: all 52 migrations baselined with zero re-runs / no collision (ledger backfilled to 52); behind-by-one applies only `library_tasks`; re-run is a clean no-op; pristine empty DB applies everything; `test:rls` 129 green. **Latent issue noted, not fixed** (belongs to Matthew, risky to touch applied history): two migrations share the prefix `20260721000600` (`firm_service_tier`, `owner_cim_visibility`) — the cross-branch timestamp collision CLAUDE.md warns about; `supabase db push` keys on version, so one of the pair may have been silently skipped in any db-push environment. No scoring/rubric/migration-set change (rules 1–6 intact). DoD: `npm run build` clean, `npm test` 355 passed / 148 skipped, `npm run test:rls` 129 passed, fresh `db:migrate` + idempotent re-run clean.

The migration drops the old `plan_template_items_kind_ref` and adds a new one that no longer admits `item_kind='playbook'`, but never removed the existing 'playbook' rows first — so ADD CONSTRAINT is validated against live pre-migration rows and fails. It passed CI only because on a fresh DB `plan_template_items` is still EMPTY at migrate time (the seed runs afterward); production had rows from a prior seed. Fix (edit to the not-yet-in-prod migration; a no-op on fresh DBs, so no divergence for envs that already applied it): before the new constraint, null the null-safe `engagement_plan_items.source_plan_template_item_id` lineage pointing at those rows (item_kind and the concrete ids are snapshotted there, so applied-plan history survives the RESTRICT FK), then `delete from plan_template_items where item_kind='playbook'`. Chose the npm-recommended `vitest@^4.1.10` (semver-major from 2.x): peer-compatible with our existing `vite ^6` and `@types/node ^22`; it dedupes the whole test tree onto the patched vite@6.4.3 and drops the separate vite-node package. - 2026-07-23 | Beta-hardening bug sweep — a cross-scope document-render leak (security) plus four correctness bugs found by a review pass over the advisor/owner/deliverables surfaces | Ran the definition-of-done suite (build, 576 vitest, RLS 134/0, migrate/seed/demo idempotent, dogfood reproduces the reference scorer, eval 8/8 — all green) then reviewed the beta-critical flows and fixed five real defects. **(1) HIGH security — `render-document-pdf` cross-scope disclosure.** The four render endpoints use `scope:'assessment'` (only checks the caller can SEE the assessment) and then `renderDocumentPdf` fetched the narrative on the SERVICE-ROLE client (RLS bypassed), so an invited collaborator or an owner could POST `{doc_type:'cim'|'teaser'|'management_presentation'|'delta_report'}` and receive a PDF RLS deliberately walls off — including an UNFINALIZED CIM draft (defeating the `owner_cim_read` finalized_at gate, docs/17). Fix: the document row is now fetched AS THE CALLER (threaded `asUser` through `HandlerArgs`→`documentPdf`→`renderDocumentPdf`→`latestNarrative`), so RLS is the authorization boundary and the exact row returned is one the caller may read — a walled doc type / unfinalized CIM yields a clean 404, staff (advisor_firm_all) are unaffected, and an owner sees the CIM only once finalized. Regression test in `tests/functions.test.ts` proves owner+collaborator are 404'd on hidden doc types with the rows present, staff get past the 404, and a finalized CIM becomes owner-visible. No scoring/rubric/RLS-policy change (rules 1–6 intact) — the fix DELEGATES to the existing policies instead of bypassing them. **(2) MEDIUM UX — RoadmapPage "generate" toast.** It counted plan-applied tasks twice (`tasksCreated` == sum of applied plans' tasks) and labeled them "from gaps" (the gap→task loop is retired), and on a no-op re-run falsely claimed "Roadmap rescheduled from the new start date" though existing tasks are never rescheduled. Toast now reports plan-applied work once and honestly says "up to date — no new plans to apply". **(3) LOW — IntakePage cleared answers.** A previously-saved answer the advisor emptied was skipped (`value===undefined → continue`), never deleted, so the DB diverged from the UI; `saveStep` now deletes cleared answers and their provenance. **(4) LOW — re-adding a soft-removed Plan.** `applyPlan`'s claim used `coalesce(engagement_plan_id, $new)`, which kept a REMOVED plan's id, stranding the tasks so the re-added plan's board group showed empty; the claim now reclaims a task when its owner is null OR removed (an active plan still keeps first-owner ownership), with a regression test in `tests/plans.test.ts`. **Surfaced, not changed (owner decisions):** (a) the entitlement gate is a no-op for `assessment`/`engagement`-scoped gated fns because those scopes resolve `firmId=null` — NOT beta-blocking (enforcement is off in the comped beta) but a GA blocker to fix before `BILLING_ENFORCED` flips; (b) two legal-page business facts still render as `[bracketed]` placeholders (mailing address, contact email) — Matthew's to supply; (c) the duplicate migration prefix `20260721000600` is already neutralized (skipped policy recreated forward in 20260722210000, firm_service_tier later dropped) and renaming applied history is riskier than leaving it. DoD green: `npm run build`, `npm test` 578 passed, `npm run test:rls` 134/0 on a clean DB, `npm run eval` 8/8, fresh migrate+seed+seed:demo idempotent.
- 2026-07-23 | Consolidation sweep + latent-bug hunt + doc alignment (parallel-agent pass) | Three coordinated passes; all code edits made serially to avoid collision. **Security (the real find) — four advisor endpoints were declared with the read-open `engagement` auth scope, which `authorize()` grants to ANY principal who can see the engagement under RLS (the owner-client and view-only external collaborators), not just firm staff.** Worst was `engagement-comparables` (HIGH): it returns SIBLING engagements across the firm — other clients' `company_name`, `industry`, `drs`, `drs_tier`, `outcome_status` — so an owner or a CPA pinned to one engagement could enumerate the firm's whole client book (latent only because its UI tab is currently commented out; the API surface was live). Also `record-deal-outcome` (an owner could set/overwrite `outcome`/`final_ev`/`multiple` on their own engagement, polluting the firm's calibration corpus and the cross-firm calibration moat), `invite-owner` (any viewer could provision arbitrary owner accounts — spam/abuse), and `generate-roadmap`. All four retargeted to `scope:'manage-engagement'` (advisor/admin profile + engagement RLS-check — the same scope `recommend-plans`/`apply-plan`/`invite-collaborator` already use); handlers are unchanged because each already resolves the firm from the engagement and ignored the context `firmId`, so this only TIGHTENS who may call, never loosens or alters behavior. Locked with a new pure (no-DB) `tests/registry.test.ts` case asserting these four are never read-open, so the scope can't silently regress. **Consolidation (safe, mechanical):** (1) `persistGeneratedDocument()` in `server/narrative.ts` — the identical fetch-firm/engagement-then-insert-into-`generated_documents` block was copied 5× (owner_report/delta/cim/teaser/management_presentation); now one helper with `doc_type`/`prompt_version`/`model` as params (a narrative table only — rule 2 intact; `doc_type` moved from a SQL literal to a bound param, behavior-identical). (3) `src/lib/workstreams.ts` local `usd()` (a near-copy of `fmtCurrencyCompact`) replaced with the shared `format.ts` helper. **Docs:** added the missing moat-3 **Engagement graph** row (`server/engagement-graph.ts` · `server/outcomes.ts`) to the docs/README feature→file map — moats 1 and 2 had rows, 3 did not though it is live code. **Surfaced, NOT changed (owner's call, deliberately left):** (a) `shared/scoring/engine.ts` has unguarded denominators (`growthInputs` base-year revenue, `depth_ratio` functional-area count, `pipeline_ratio` last-year revenue) that yield `Infinity`→top band on a zero input — NOT touched because it's the deterministic scorer (rule 1) and a guard must be mirrored in `seed/fixtures/reference_scorer.py` and re-fixtured, and "what should a zero-base-year revenue score" is a methodology question (Matthew); needs confirmation of whether question validation guarantees positivity. (d) Proposed a narrow `resolveEngagementFirm(db,id)` server helper for the ~5 pure "just need the firm_id from the engagement" reads — left as a propose-and-confirm since these reads sit at the authorization boundary. Also recommend adding an owner-JWT-403 regression on the three write endpoints to `scripts/rls-test.ts` (needs a live DB to author/verify). No scoring/rubric/schema/RLS-policy change (rules 1–6 intact) — the security fix delegates to existing scopes, the rest is refactor + docs. - 2026-07-23 | Fix "The CAPTCHA failed to load" on the Clerk sign-up page | The hosted `<SignUp>` (src/pages/SignUpPage.tsx) surfaced Clerk's bot-protection error "The CAPTCHA failed to load. - 2026-07-23 | Guard against migration-version collisions in CI (tests/migrations.test.ts) — the Supabase-CI failure mode that already bit us once | Investigated a reported "Supabase failing CI": reproduced the full ci.yml pipeline locally against a fresh Postgres 16 (migrate → test:rls 134/0 → seed×2 → seed:demo×2 reconciling the reference scorer → npm test → eval 8/8 → build) — all green, and the last 30 CI runs were green. - 2026-07-23 | Compliance pack: make the document-vs-structured-data encryption scope explicit | Follow-up to the SOC 2 pack. A reviewer asked whether DB datapoints are encrypted or just documents; the honest answer is that only uploaded document bytes carry app-level AES-256-GCM (key in EB_DOCUMENT_KEY, outside the data plane — server/documents/crypto.ts + storage.ts), while structured datapoints (assessment answers, financial summaries, owner PFR inputs, DRS/ORI scores, profile PII) are ordinary Postgres columns protected by Supabase volume encryption at rest + RLS + TLS, NOT field-level encrypted (verified: no pgcrypto/Vault/pgsodium in the schema). This is a standard, audit-accepted architecture (SOC 2 doesn't require field-level encryption of queryable data), but the pack lumped both NPI forms together. Added an "Encryption scope — documents vs. structured data" subsection to policy 08 with a per-form table, the plainly-stated residual (a DB-layer compromise exposes structured NPI but not document contents), and the deliberately-not-adopted field-encryption enhancement (KMS/Vault) rationale; tightened the at-rest bullet. Split the evidence-index at-rest row into documents (app-level ✅) vs structured (volume ✅ / field 🟡). Tightened both C1.1 rows (readiness assessment + TSC matrix) so "NPI encrypted at rest" can't be misread as field-level. Added risk-register R17 (Confidentiality, treatment Accept) for the residual. Docs-only; no scoring/rubric/schema/RLS/source change (rules 1–6 intact).
- 2026-07-23 | DRS scoring stress test → shipped input-validation guard (crashes/silent-corruption) + wrote a methodology remediation plan for ratification | Started from a narrow product question (how to treat 1–2-year-old businesses we want to retain) but first stress-tested the WHOLE deterministic model: 12 business-archetype agents built and EMPIRICALLY scored real companies through the actual engine logic (a Python harness validated to reproduce all three canonical fixtures exactly), then a synthesis ranked and deduped the findings. The young-business case turned out to be the LOWEST-severity finding; the test surfaced (a) six engine crash/silent-corruption classes and (b) whole mis-tiered business classes. **SHIPPED (Part 1, correctness only — not a methodology change):** `validateAnswers()` in `shared/scoring/engine.ts` (called by `scoreFromAnswers` after the completeness check) + a mirrored `validate()` in `seed/fixtures/reference_scorer.py`, because the engine did no input validation and did not crash on ordinary inputs — it SILENTLY produced meaningless scores (a $0 opening-revenue year scored "Institutional Grade" via Infinity CAGR; a solo with OPS-FUNC-COUNT=0 got a perfect management-depth ratio; a single fiscal year produced a bogus CAGR; negative churn scored 100; an out-of-range 1–5 scale pushed ORI to 139; an empty customer-share list swallowed NaN). This closes the exact unguarded-denominator deferral logged in the 2026-07-23 consolidation sweep, by taking the REJECT-INVALID-INPUT path (guards: ≥2 strictly-positive revenue years; customer shares a non-empty ≤5 list each 0–100 summing ≤100; core-function count ≥1; 1–5 scales in range; selects within options; no negative numerics). Validation only — a well-formed assessment's score is unchanged, so the fixtures are byte-identical and rule #1 holds; 13 guard cases added to `tests/engine.test.ts`. **PROPOSED (Part 3, awaiting Matthew's band-by-band ratification — NOT built):** new `docs/drs-scoring-stress-test-and-remediation-plan.md` details the fixable scoring bugs (endpoint-only CAGR trajectory-blindness; concentration bands saturating so a single-customer business reaches "Sale Ready"; recurring-revenue bias locking transactional/project/asset/practice models out of Institutional Grade; solo/owner-operator floors + a ~15pt gaming premium; NRR-"unknown" scored at the worst band and beatable by fabrication; false/mislabeled gaps; the pipeline construct; `GRW-POS` capped at 80; and the young-company/mature-business age caps — the original question, to be fixed via the neutralize-&-re-normalize mechanic Matthew chose, as a new rubric_version) and separates them from the by-design limits where the standalone-EBITDA DRS structurally cannot see IP/asset/market-timing/license value (a product-scope decision), whose one in-scope bridge is that the tier labels/gap sets still over-claim and can INVERT (a 95.1 "Institutional Grade, zero gaps" on a CON/Medicare-license-fragile surgery center) — fixable by scoping labels to "standalone operational readiness" + blind-spot flags. Reverted pre-existing seed drift the regeneration surfaced (hand-enriched playbooks/content-modules) to keep the diff focused; fixtures unchanged. DoD: `npm run build` clean, `npm test` 434 passed / 161 skipped (+13 guard cases; scoring engine still reproduces fixtures — rule 1). - 2026-07-23 | DRS-2.0 methodology upgrade — the ratified remediation of the scoring stress test (10 decisions, one new rubric_version) | Following the stress test (see docs/drs-scoring-stress-test-and-remediation-plan.md), Matthew ratified all proposed methodology changes ("yes to all, don't overfit"); every band is grounded in LMM M&A methodology, not the synthetic stress-test companies (which only detect breakage). Shipped as **DRS-2.0** (RUBRIC_VERSION_LABEL bump), with the reference scorer, the four→seven fixtures, and the test suite kept in lockstep (rule 1) — every change was designed so the all-applicable path is bit-identical to DRS-1.0, so mature businesses are untouched and only the intended cases move. **Foundation:** a data-driven `na_when` applicability concept (business_age_lt / history_years_lt / employee_count_lte / answer_unknown / answer_in) — a Not-Applicable sub-score is excluded from its dimension, which re-normalizes over the remaining weights (methodology stays in the rubric, rule 3); a gap keyed on an N/A sub-score cannot fire. **The ten decisions:** D9 age-aware (BIZ-AGE-YEARS input; tenure/growth-history/retention/valuation N/A when too young; STALE_VALUATION age-gated via new business_age_gte trigger) — the original question, and the lowest-impact finding. D5 NRR "unknown" excluded+re-normalized instead of worst-band, CHURN_HIGH decoupled. D10 GRW-POS ceiling 80→100. D3 revenue-model branch (REV-MODEL input; REV-RECUR/DURABILITY/NRR N/A for transactional/asset-rental) so transactional/project/rental businesses aren't capped below Institutional by model design. D1 graded negative growth bands (soft/eroding/melting) replacing the single hard-zero, data-driven in GRW-CAGR bands. D2 concentration gradient extended across 40–100%, an anchor offset (a contractually locked-in dominant customer floors at 45), and a governor (unprotected top-1 ≥50% caps DRS at 69 — concentration otherwise reaches only ~14.5% of the DRS, so bands alone can't hold a single-customer business below Sale Ready). D8 pipeline coverage vs the AVERAGE of the provided years (kills collapse-inflation) + graded 0.5x credit + PIPELINE_BLIND suppressed for recurring/asset models (new answer_not_in trigger). D7 gap relabels (REV_VOLATILITY→"Weak Revenue Growth", CONTRACT_GAP→"Weak Contract Coverage"; structural suppressions already handled by the N/A mechanism). D6 blind-spot flags + standalone-readiness framing (new OPS-LICENSE-DEP input + existing VAL-ASSETS-CTX raise flags when license/CON transferability or asset/IP value sits outside the model, so a high score never reads as "no risks" on a value-fragile business — the fix for the ASC-scores-95-with-zero-gaps inversion; tier strings unchanged to avoid UI/narrative ripple). D4 owner-operator branch (EMPLOYEE-COUNT input; OPS-DEPTH/MGT-LAYERS/MGT-NC/MGT-RETENTION N/A for ≤3 non-owner employees so solos aren't floored to Not Saleable; headcount-consistency validation + neutralization kill the ~15pt gaming premium; SDE/transition flag reframes the value basis). New persisted `applicable` column on sub_score_results (default true) so the advisory library ignores non-applicable sub-scores. New fixtures: young SaaS (71.6, was penalized), transactional job shop (71.5, was capped), anchor-protected aerospace supplier (71.9), solo CPA (67.9, was Not Saleable). Out of scope by design (Part 4, future product decision): valuing IP/asset-floor/market-timing/strategic-synergy — the DRS remains a standalone-EBITDA operational index. DoD: `npm run build` clean, `npm test` 472 passed / 161 skipped (all seven fixtures reproduce the reference scorer exactly — rule 1). RLS/db-migrate/seed run in CI (need a live DB); the one new migration (sub_score_applicable) is additive and the naming guard passes.
- 2026-07-23 | Fix re-seed FK violation — engagement_plan_items lineage now ON DELETE SET NULL | `npm run db:seed` failed on any database with an applied engagement plan ("update or delete on table plan_template_items violates foreign key constraint engagement_plan_items_source_plan_template_item_id_fkey"): server/seed-methodology.ts clears and rebuilds every SYSTEM plan's items on each seed (`delete from plan_template_items where firm_id is null`), but engagement_plan_items.source_plan_template_item_id referenced those rows via an FK created with the default NO ACTION (20260721000100_plans.sql), so the delete was blocked. The column is documented as "null-safe" template lineage (docs/37 line 214, docs/02) — the concrete rows an applied plan produced (task_id/milestone_id/content/advisory ids) and item_kind are snapshotted on the engagement_plan_items row, so applied-plan history survives a template item deletion — which is exactly ON DELETE SET NULL semantics the original FK omitted. New migration (20260723232946_plan_template_item_lineage_on_delete_set_null.sql) drops and re-adds the FK with ON DELETE SET NULL, promoting to a schema guarantee the manual null-out the playbook-retirement migration (20260722202931) already did by hand before deleting, and fixing the identical latent violation in the draft-Plan edit path (server/plans.ts `delete from plan_template_items where plan_template_id = $1`). Verified against a fresh Postgres 16: the NO ACTION FK reproduces the exact reported error, ON DELETE SET NULL lets the re-seed succeed while preserving the applied-plan row + its item_kind snapshot and severing only the lineage pointer to null. No scoring/rubric/RLS/AI change (rules 1-6 intact); base migration left untouched (immutable history). DoD: `npm run build` clean, `npm test` 649 passed, `npm run test:rls` 139/0, fresh migrate + idempotent seed (re-seed with a live engagement plan item now succeeds).
- 2026-07-23 | Make the methodology-load row-count check rubric-version-aware (stop false-failing after a version bump) | After the FK re-seed fix landed, "Load methodology" ran cleanly but reported spurious count mismatches on any database seeded before the DRS-1.0→2.0 bump: rubric_versions 2/1, dimensions 18/9, questions 112/58, sub_scores 64/32, gap_definitions 48/24, gap_plan_map 48/24, gap_content_map 88/44. Root cause is expected accumulation, not corruption — rubric_versions upserts on version_label (server/seed-methodology.ts), so a label bump inserts a NEW version plus a fresh set of its (rubric_version_id, code)-keyed children, and the prior version's rows are RETAINED on purpose (rule 4: versions are immutable and each assessment pins the one it was scored under, so old rows must stay readable). The verification's raw unfiltered count(*) therefore grows by a full methodology every bump. Fix scopes the count for the seven rubric-versioned tables to the current rubric_version (fetched by RUBRIC_VERSION_LABEL after commit, since the txn's id is out of scope; dimensions/gap_definitions by rubric_version_id, questions/sub_scores via their dimension, gap_plan/content_map via their gap_definition; a fallback zero-UUID makes a never-seeded DB count 0 = a real loud failure). Tenant-bearing tables keep their firm_id-null filter; non-versioned tables are unchanged, so GENUINE drift still flags — verified an orphan advisory_library_items row still reports 40/39 MISMATCH (the 15 stale system advisory items on the reporting DB are real orphan drift, deliberately left per Matthew: cleaning them needs the same ON DELETE SET NULL treatment on engagement_plan_items.advisory_library_item_id and is out of this change's scope). Verification-only; no data/methodology/schema/RLS/AI change (rules 1-6 intact); DRS-1.0 rows confirmed retained. Empirically reproduced the user's two-version state (cloned the rubric graph under a DRS-1.0 label → 18 dimensions/48 gaps) and confirmed the re-seed now reports every rubric table at its single-version count while the old version persists. DoD: npm run build clean, npm test 649 passed, npm run test:rls 139/0, fresh migrate + seed clean.
- 2026-07-23 | Harden the QuickBooks upload autofill against real QBO CSV exports (server/pl-extract.ts) | The "Fill financials from a P&L" panel (PLImportPanel → extract-financials-from-file → extractFinancials) was tested against a clean fixture but broke on files QuickBooks Online actually exports. Six deterministic robustness fixes, still no LLM and still write-nothing (rules 1–2 intact — the extractor only PROPOSES answers a human applies via enter-manual-financials): **(1) BOM.** Strip a leading UTF-8 BOM from CSV and JSON text (QBO/Excel exports carry one; it corrupted the first cell and broke JSON.parse). **(2) Preamble.** Skip the company/"Profit and Loss"/date-range title rows and detect the real header as the first multi-COLUMN row (keyed on column count + one non-empty cell, so a `,Total` header with a blank first cell is found and a `,,,,` spacer is not) — previously row 0 (the company name) was assumed to be the header, defeating year detection. **(3) Total column.** Drop a trailing "Total" summary column (header normalizes to exactly "total") from the period set — a QBO comparison P&L appends one, and left in it was read as the most-recent fiscal year, silently overstating current-year revenue. **(4) Roll-up vs sub-account.** Reordered REVENUE_LABELS so every "Total …" section-total (incl. "Total Income", the QBO default revenue roll-up) outranks bare account lines ("Sales"/"Income"), and a revenue row is only accepted if it actually carries a figure — so an indented "Product Sales" sub-line no longer beats "Total Income", and a blank "Income" group-header row is skipped. Recurring % is now cross-footed against the SAME period column as the most-recent revenue. **(5) Monthly P&L.** When ≥2 period columns all fall in one fiscal year (a monthly/quarterly P&L), warn and mark the result non-verifiable (records self_reported, not document-verified) instead of mislabeling months as fiscal years. **(6) Customer $ column.** Revenue-by-customer concentration now falls back to a dollar amount column (QBO "Sales by Customer Summary" reports totals, not %), computing shares from the summed non-aggregate customers. Also: clearer error hinting Export → CSV when an .xlsx/.xls/.pdf is uploaded (extractor + PLImportPanel). Presentation/parse only — no scoring/rubric/schema/RLS/AI change. DoD: `npm run build` clean, `npm test` 493 passed / 161 skipped (+6 QBO-shape cases in tests/pl-extract.test.ts: BOM, preamble+Total-column+Total-Income roll-up, monthly-P&L warning, JSON BOM, xlsx hint, customer dollar-column). (test:rls/db:migrate unaffected — pure parser change, no DB/eval touch.)
- 2026-07-23 | Prune orphaned system advisory_library_items on re-seed (FK-safe) | The methodology load reported advisory_library_items 54/39 — 15 stale SYSTEM rows (firm_id null) whose codes were dropped from the seed file but never cleaned up, because advisory_library_items lacked the orphan cleanup library_tasks already has. Added that cleanup: after the advisory upsert, `delete from advisory_library_items where firm_id is null and code not in (current seed codes) and not referenced by any plan_template_items`. Two FKs point at this table with NO ACTION, handled differently by design: (a) engagement_plan_items.advisory_library_item_id — made ON DELETE SET NULL (new migration 20260723235154), the same null-safe-snapshot rationale as the plan-template lineage fix (item_kind is snapshotted, so applied history survives the pointer going null); (b) plan_template_items.advisory_library_item_id — deliberately KEPT NO ACTION, because that table's kind_ref check requires the column NOT NULL for item_kind='advisory' (SET NULL would violate the check), so the cleanup's `not exists (plan_template_items ...)` guard skips any advisory item a plan template still references. Safe because system plan items are cleared up front and rebuilt referencing only current advisory codes, so the only plan_template_items that can reference an orphan at cleanup time are FIRM plans, which are correctly preserved. Verified on a fresh DB with three planted orphans: unreferenced orphan deleted; orphan referenced by a live engagement_plan_item deleted with the pointer SET NULL and the row + item_kind='advisory' retained; orphan referenced by a firm plan_template_item skipped/kept. Idempotent re-seed on a clean DB is a no-op (advisory 39/39). Seed + one additive FK migration; no scoring/rubric/RLS/AI change (rules 1-6 intact). DoD: npm run build clean, npm test 649 passed, npm run test:rls 139/0, fresh migrate + seed + idempotent re-seed clean.

- 2026-07-24 | Research: benchmarking/aggregate-data interaction, own-book×paid-data blend, buy-vs-pass-through (docs/sellside-ai/04) | Matthew asked how users should interact with benchmarking/aggregate data, how the firm own book blends with paid datasets, and whether we pass through client subscriptions or pay. Wrote docs/sellside-ai/04-benchmarking-data-interaction.md (design record, no code). Key framing: (1) disentangle three pools — licensed `market` (bought, non-tenant, no moat, vendor $$$), firm own-book (deal_outcomes→ownBookMultiple, firm-scoped, per-firm moat, free), cross-firm `analytics` pool (de-identified, service-role only, THE moat, free/ours) — the pass-vs-pay question is about the licensed pool ONLY. (2) Interaction: benchmark is a deterministic LENS on the score (percentile via quantile(), rule #1-safe), never a second number; every cell shows n/as_of/source; k-anonymity small-cell suppression on the cross-firm pool; advisor-rich vs owner-curated; read-only, recalibration ships as a new rubric_version. (3) Blend: evolve selectValuationMultiple from strict-precedence cliff to a deterministic confidence-weighted blend (market cold-start → own-book refinement → calibration overlay), versioned, disabled-by-default; blend at SELECTION time, never merge datasets (would breach vendor terms + taint moat). (4) Buy-vs-pass-through = the rule-#1 lane split IS the commercial split: platform-PAY to OWN the Feist-unprotectable facts (deterministic multiple lane, cheap aggregate tier, can seed the moat); PASS-THROUGH the firm own license or a paid per-firm entitlement for copyrightable row-level comps/verbatim passages (RAG lane, expensive redistribution/display tier). Rides the existing entitlements gate + market.datasets exposure flags; never pool pass-through vendor data into the cross-firm moat. Open calls flagged as Matthew/counsel-owned (docs/41 §7/§8). Also updated docs/sellside-ai/README.md (now four writeups).

- 2026-07-24 | Consolidate the 3 duplicated generation pipelines into one intelligence runtime (docs/sellside-ai/05, Phase A) | An inventory found the reasoning runtime implemented THREE times (not two): server/narrative.ts, server/diligence-simulation.ts, server/institutional-review.ts each carried a near-identical private callClaude, numeral-firewall generate loop (resolvePrompt→generate→numeralPostCheck→one regen→throw), pick/fallback contract (AI path OR aiFailureReason-warn→deterministic composer OR composer), and DRAFT_BANNER/withDraftBanner; institutional-review even used literal PROMPT_VERSION/MODEL constants instead of the agent registry. STRICTLY byte-identical: the numeral-firewall whitelist moved from the payload object to the caller's userContent string (= prefix + JSON.stringify(payload, null, 2)) whose extracted numeral SET is identical, so injected-generator regen tests and every output are unchanged. This is the foundation for Diligence Q&A (Phase B), which gets the no-credit fallback for free by supplying a retrieval-only composer. (4) `.claude/settings.json` — wires the hook + a permission allowlist for the definition-of-done and safe dev/git commands (fewer prompts). (5) `.claude/commands/{dod,db-up}.md` — `/dod` runs the whole gate in the CI-correct order, `/db-up` forces DB readiness now. (6) `.claude/README.md` documents it; `.gitignore` now keeps local skill/plugin installs ignored (`.claude/*`) while committing the shared infra; one pointer bullet added to CLAUDE.md. Pure session ergonomics — no app/scoring/schema/RLS/AI change (rules 1-6 untouched). Verified end-to-end from zero manual setup: hook emits valid SessionStart JSON; bootstrap installs deps + applies all 68 migrations to a fresh DB + seeds; `npm run build` clean; `npm test` 709 passed/82 files (DB-backed tests now RUN against the seeded dev DB rather than skipping); test:rls 143 passed/0 failed on the clean throwaway DB.
- 2026-07-24 | UI copy audit: institutional register, em dashes removed from user-facing narrative | Swept every advisor/owner/platform page, domain component, shared UI primitive, and rendered lib string. Removed the rhetorical em dash (the #1 AI-verbose tell) from user-facing copy, replacing it with the punctuation the sentence needs (period/comma/colon) or the app's `·` separator idiom; also trimmed hedges ("simply", hype metaphors). Two conventions were explicitly protected and left untouched: the standalone `'—'` null-value placeholder in tables/stats (financial convention), and all code comments. Legal copy (pages/legal/content.ts) was out of scope. Copy-only: `npm run build` and `npm test` (540 scoring tests) stay green. Structural flow findings (missing "Stage 2" label in the evidence flow, VerifyPage/VerificationPage name collision, a few duplicated subtitles, the rubric.ts CLI-instruction error string) are recorded in the PR body for Matthew, not auto-fixed.
- 2026-07-24 | UI refinement via Impeccable audit: decorative left-accent stripes removed; colored left rail now signals status/severity only | Ran Paul Bakaus' open-source `impeccable` design skill (github.com/pbakaus/impeccable) detector over `src/`. It surfaced 14 findings; triaged and acted on them without churn, keeping the fixes inside the app's own institutional register (docs/26 §"Border-defined elevation" / "the accent is spent, not smeared"). CHANGED (removed the `side-tab` AI-tell — a thick colored border on one side of a bordered surface — leaving the uniform 1px hairline the design system already prescribes): `.login-notice`, `.wb-explainer`, `.consensus-callout`, `.ws-chip` (its rail was always `--status-neutral`; state is already shown by `.ws-chip-step`/`.ws-chip-dot`, so the rail was pure decoration). `.login-devnote` and `.dev-note` were left-bar text asides; refined to contained notes (hairline + `--radius-sm` + `--surface-2`), matching `.login-notice`. KEPT + documented with the tool's own inline `impeccable-disable-line` waivers (so a future `impeccable detect` passes clean with recorded intent) the left rails that ENCODE DATA, not decoration: `.ui-toast` (good/error status), `.advisory-item` + its mobile card + `.dsim-finding` (critical/high/med/low severity). Net effect: a colored left rail in the app now means exactly one thing — this element carries a status or severity — which tightens the visual language rather than just muting it. Also documented the three progress-fill `transition: width` findings (`.intake-progress-fill`, `.verif-fill`, `.plan-progress-fill`) as intentional: they are one-shot meter fills inside `overflow:hidden` pill tracks, and the suggested `transform:scaleX` would distort the rounded caps. Fixed one detector false positive by rewording a doc comment in `src/lib/supabase.ts` that literally contained `<img>`. Presentational-only: no schema, scoring engine, RLS policy, or narrative code touched, so rules 1-6 hold untouched and the RLS/fresh-DB/eval gates are unaffected. `impeccable detect src/` now exits 0. DoD: `npm run build` clean; `npm test` 765 passed.
- 2026-07-24 | Fix "AI returns no output" + consolidate the LLM call path + clean the copilot fallback surface | Diagnosis from the gateway dashboard: calls reached the right models (anthropic/claude-opus-4.8, anthropic/claude-haiku-4.5) but returned 0 output tokens — server/intelligence/runtime.ts callClaude sent `thinking: { type: 'adaptive' }`, which can come back with only a thinking block and no text, so callClaude threw "returned no text" and every path silently degraded to its composer/fallback (which is also why Copilot showed the raw-tool fallback). Three coordinated changes. (1) CONSOLIDATE: one `createMessage()` + `messageText()` in server/llm/provider.ts is now the ONLY place a Messages request is built — plain generation, no `thinking` config, model id namespaced once. The three former call sites (runtime.ts callClaude, copilot.ts defaultTransport, llm/client.ts anthropicTransport) all route through it, so the request shape can't drift. max output capped at 8192 (every configured model supports it; a report/CIM section fits) to remove any over-limit-max_tokens rejection. (2) DIAGNOSABILITY: callClaude's empty-completion error now names the stop_reason + content block types, so a future "no text" is legible instead of silent. (3) CLEAN AI SURFACE: the advisor-copilot deterministic fallback no longer dumps ```json blobs — a new shape-agnostic renderer prints readable markdown (Title-Cased field labels, bullet lists, object one-line summaries, capped long arrays, em-dash nulls), and each tool carries an optional human `label`. No rule-1/2 change: the numeral firewall and citation contract are unchanged; this only fixes HOW the model is called and HOW a fallback reads. DoD: build clean; npm test 765/765 (serial); npm run eval 8/8 + bench owner_report & diligence_qa 100%/100%; test:rls 145/0.
